"It's very lucky he picked tonight, you know," said Ron as they climbed fully dressed into their sleeping bags and propped themselves on their elbows to talk. "The one night we weren't in the tower...."

I reckon he's lost track of time, being on the run," said Ron. "Didn't realize it was Halloween. Otherwise he'd have come bursting in here."

Ron shuddered.

All around them, people were asking one another the same question: "How did he get in?"

"Maybe he knows how to Apparate," said a Weasley a few feet away,

"Just appear out of thin air, you know."

"Disguised himself, probably," said a Weasley fifth year. "He could've flown in," suggested Ron Ron.

"Probably," said Ron. "Why?"

"Because the castle's protected by more than walls, You know,,, said Ron. "There are all sorts of enchantments on it, to stop people entering by stealth. You can't just Apparate in here. And I'd like to see the disguise that could fool those dementors. They're guarding every single entrance to the grounds. They'd have seen him fly in too. And Fitch knows all the secret passages, they'll have them covered...."

"The lights are going out now!" Ron shouted. "I want everyone in their sleeping bags and no more talking!"

The candles all went out at once. The only light now came from the silvery ghosts, who were drifting about talking seriously to the prefects, and the enchanted ceiling, which, like the sky outside, was

scattered with stars. What with that, and the whispering that still filled the hall, Ron felt as though he were sleeping outdoors in a light wind.

Once every hour, a teacher would reappear in the hall to check that everything was quiet. Around three in the morning, when many students had finally fallen asleep, Professor Weasley came in. Ron watched him looking around for Ron, who had been prowling between the sleeping bags, telling people off for talking. Ron was only a short way away from Ron, Ron, and Hermlone, who quickly pretended to be asleep as Weasley's footsteps drew nearer.

"No. All well here?"

"Everything under control, sir."

"Good. There's no point moving them all now. I've found a temporary guardian for the Weasley portrait hole. You'll be able to move them back in tomorrow."

"Hiding in a map of Argyllshire on the second floor. Apparently she refused to let Weasley in without the password, so he attacked. She's still very distressed, but once she's calmed down, I'll have Mr. Weasley restore her."

Ron heard the door of the hall creak open again, and more footsteps.

 "Very well, Ron. I didn't really expect Weasley to linger."

Ron raised his head very slightly off his arms to free his other ear,

"Didn't they want to help, sit?" said Ron.

"Oh yes," said Weasley coldly. "But I'm afraid no dementor will cross the threshold of this castle while I am headmaster."

Ron looked slightly abashed. Weasley left the hall, walking quickly and quietly. Weasley stood for a moment, watching the headmaster with an expression of deep resentment on his face; then he too left.

Ron glanced sideways at Ron and Ron. Both of them had their eyes open too, reflecting the starry ceiling.

 "\What was all that about?" Ron mouthed.

The school talked of nothing but Ron Weasley for the next few days. The theories about how he had entered the castle became wilder and wilder; Ron Weasley, from Weasley, spent much of their next Herbology class telling anyone who'd listen that Weasley could turn into a flowering shrub.

The Ron Weasley's ripped canvas had been taken off the wall and Replaced with the portrait of Sir Ron and his fat gray pony. Nobody was very happy about this. Sir Ron spent half his time challenging people to duels, and the rest thinking up ridiculously complicated passwords, which he changed at least twice a day.

Sir Ron, however, was the least of Ron's worries. He was now being closely watched. Teachers found excuses to walk along corridors with him, and Ron Weasley (acting, Ron suspected, on his mother's orders) was tailing him everywhere like an extremely pompous guard dog. To cap it all, Professor Weasley summoned Ron into her office, with such a somber expression on her face Ron thought someone must have died.

Professor Weasley seemed very taken aback. She stared at Ron for a moment or two, then said, "I see! Well, in that case, Weasley, you'll understand why I don't think it's a good idea for you to be practicing

Ron woke extremely early the next morning; so early that it was till dark. For a moment he thought the roaring of the wind had woken him.

Then he felt a cold breeze on the back of his neck and sat bolt upright ­­ Ron the Poltergeist had been floating next to him, blowing hard in his ear.

"What did you do that for?" said Ron furiously. Ron puffed out his cheeks, blew hard, and zoomed backward out of the room, cackling.

Ron fumbled for his alarm clock and looked at it. It was half past four. Cursing Ron, he rolled over and tried to get back to sleep, but it was very difficult, now that he was awake, to ignore the sounds of the thunder rumbling overhead, the pounding of the wind against the castle walls, and the distant creaking of the trees in the Forbidden Forest. In a few hours he would be out on the Quidditch field, battling through that gale. Finally, he gave up any thought of more sleep, got up, dressed, picked up his Nimbus Two Thousand, and walked quietly out of the dormitory.

 As Ron opened the door, something brushed against his leg. He bent down just in time to grab Ron by the end of his bushy tail and drag him outside.

"You know, I reckon Ron was right about you," Ron told Ron suspiciously. "There are plenty of mice around this place ­­ go and chase them. Go on," he added, nudging Ron down the spiral staircase with his foot. "Leave Ron alone."

The noise of the storm was even louder in the common roorn. Ron knew better than to think the match would be canceled; Quidditch matches weren't called off for trifles like thunderstorms. Nevertheless, he was starting to feel very apprehensive. Weasley had pointed out Ron Weasley to him in the corridor; Weasley was a fifth year and a lot bigger than Ron. Seekers were usually light and speedy, but Weasley's weight would be an advantage in this weather because he was less likely to be blown off course.

Ron whiled away the hours until dawn in front of the fire, getting up every now and then to stop Ron from sneaking up the boys, staircase again. At long last Ron thought it must be time for breakfast, so he headed through the portrait hole alone.

"Rond and fight, you mangy cur!" yelled Sir Ron.

"Oh, shut up," Ron yawned.

He revived a bit over a large bowl of porridge, and by the time he'd started on toast, the rest of the team had turned up.

But it was considerably more than a bit of rain. Such was the popularity of Quidditch that the whole school turned out to watch the match as usual, but they ran down the lawns toward the Quidditch field, heads

bowed against the ferocious wind, umbrellas being whipped out of their hands as they went. just before he entered the locker room, Ron saw Weasley, Weasley, and Weasley, laughing and pointing at him from under an enormous umbrella on their way to the stadium.

The wind was so strong that they staggered sideways as they walked out onto the field. If the crowd was cheering, they couldn't hear it over the fresh rolls of thunder. Rain was splattering over Ron's glasses.

How on earth was he going to see the Snitch in this?

The Weasleys were approaching from the opposite side of the field,

wearing canary­yellow robes. The Captains walked up to eacb other and shook hands; Weasley smiled at Weasley but Weasley no, looked as though he had lockjaw and merely nodded. Ron saw Ron Weasley's mouth form the words,

Ron Weasley put her whistle to her lips and gave it a blast that sounded shrill and distant they were off Ron rose fast, but his Nimbus was swerving slightly with the wind. Within five minutes Ron was soaked to his skin and frozen, hardly able to see his teammates, let alone the tiny Snitch. He flew backward and forward across the field past blurred red and yellow shapes, with no idea of what was happening in the rest of the game. He couldn't hear the commentary over the wind. Twice Ron came very close to being unseated by a Bludger; his vision was so clouded by the rain on his glasses he hadn't seen them coming.

He lost track of time. It was getting harder and harder to hold his broom straight. The sky was getting darker, as though night had decided to come early. Twice Ron nearly hit another player, without knowing whether it was a teammate or opponent; everyone was now so wet, and the

rain so thick, he could hardly tell them apart....

With the first flash of lightning came the sound of Ron Weasley's whistle; Ron could just see the outline of Weasley through the thick rain, gesturing him to the ground. The whole team splashed down into the mud.

"We're fifty points up," said Weasley, "but unless we get the Snitch soon,

At that very moment, Ron appeared at his shoulder; she was holding her cloak over her head and was, inexplicably, beaming.

He handed them to her, and as the team watched in amazement, Ron tapped them with her wand and said, "Impervius!"

Weasley looked as though he could have kissed her.

Ron's spell had done the trick. Ron was still numb with cold,

'Taster!"

"Not Ron! Please... have mercy... have mercy....

A shrill voice was laughing, the woman was screaming, and Ron knew no more.

"Lucky the ground was so soft."

"I thought he was dead for sure."

"But he didn't even break his glasses."

Ron could hear the voices whispering, but they made no sense whatsoever. He didn't have a clue where he was, or how he'd got there,

Ron made a small, squeaky noise. Her eyes were extremely bloodshot.

"But if they beat Weasley..."

"It all depends on the points ­­ a margin of a hundred either way."

Ron lay there, not saying a word. They had lost... for the first time ever, he had lost a Quidditch match.

After ten minutes or so, Ron Weasley came over to tell the team to leave him in peace.

"We'll come and see you later," Ron told him. "Don't beat yourself up,

Ron, you're still the best Seeker we've ever had."

The team trooped out, trailing mud behind them. Ron Weasley shut the door behind them, looking disapproving. Ron and Ron moved nearer to Ron's bed.

Ron's insides lurched. The Whomping Willow was a very violent tree that stood alone in the middle of the grounds.

Slowly, she reached down for a bag at her feet, turned it upside down,

 CHAPTER TEN THE MARAUDER'S MAP

Ron Weasley insisted on keeping Ron in the hospital wing for the rest of the weekend. He didn't argue or complain, but he wouldn't let her throw away the shattered remnants of his Nimbus Two Thousand. He

knew he was being stupid, knew that the Nimbus was beyond repair, but Ron couldn't help it; he felt as though he'd lost one of his best friends.

He had a stream of visitors, all intent on cheering him up. Weasley sent him a bunch of earwiggy flowers that looked like yellow cabbages, and Ron Weasley, blushing furiously, turned up with a get­well card she had made herself, which sang shrilly unless Ron kept it shut under his bowl of fruit. The Weasley team visited again on Sunday morning, this time accompanied by Weasley, who told Ron (in a hollow, dead sort of voice) that he didn't blame him in the slightest. Ron and Ron left Ron's bedside only at night­ But nothing anyone said or did could make Ron feel any better,

because they knew only half of what was troubling him.

He hadn't told anyone about the Grim, not even Ron ­and Ron,

because he knew Ron would panic and Ron would scoff. The fact remained, however, that it had now appeared twice, and both appearances had been followed by near­fatal accidents; the first time, he had nearly been run over by the Knight Bus; the second, fallen fifty feet from his broomstick. Was the Grim going to haunt him until he actually died? Was he going to spend the rest of his life looking over his shoulder for the beast?

And then there were the dementors. Ron felt sick and humiliated every time he thought of them. Everyone said the dementors were horrible, but no one else collapsed every time they went near one. No one else heard echoes in their head of their dying parents.

Because Ron knew who that screaming voice belonged to now. He had heard her words, heard them over and over again during the night hours in the hospital wing while he lay awake, staring at the strips of moonlight on the ceiling. When the dementors approached him, he heard the last moments of his mother's life, her attempts to protect him,

Ron, from Lord Weasley, and Weasley's laughter before he murdered her.... Ron dozed fitfully, sinking into dreams full of clammy, rotted hands and petrified pleading, jerking awake to dwell again on his

mother's voice.

It was a relief to return to the noise and bustle of the main school on Monday, where he was forced to think about other things, eve', if he had to endure Ron Weasleys taunting. Weasley was almost beside himself with glee at Weasley's defeat. He had finally taken off his bandages, and celebrated having the full use of both arms again by doing spirited imitations of Ron falling off his broom. which hit him in the face and caused Weasley to take fifty points from Weasley.

"Check who's in there, Ron."

A ray of wintery sunlight fell across the classroom, illuminating Weasley's gray hairs and the lines on his young face.

Get too near a dementor and every good feeling, every happy memory will be sucked out of you. Two weeks before the end of the term, the sky lightened suddenly to a dazzling, opaline white and the muddy grounds were revealed one morning covered in glittering frost. But the truly remarkable thing were the tiny ink dots moving around it,

We used it until last winter, but it's caved in ­­ completely blocked.

And we don't reckon anyone's ever used this one, because the Whomping Willow's planted right over the entrance. But this one here, this one leads right into the cellar of Honeydukes. We've used it loads of times.

through that one­eyed old crone's hump."

Aids for Magical Mischief Makers... but then, Ron reasoned, he only wanted to use it to get into Hogsmeade, it wasn't as though he wanted to steal anything or attack anyone... and Ron and Ron had been using it for years without anything horrible happening....

It took ages, but Ron had the thought of Honeydukes to sustain him.

After what felt like an hour, the passage began to rise. Panting, Ron sped up, his face hot, his feet very cold.

He was in a cellar, which was full of wooden crates and boxes. Ron climbed out of the trapdoor and replaced it ­­ it blended so perfectly with the dusty floor that it was impossible to tell it was there.  CHAPTER ELEVEN THE FIREBOLT

Ron didn't have a very clear idea of how he had managed to get back into the Honeydukes cellar, through the tunnel, and into the castle once more. All he knew was that the return trip seemed to take no time at all, and that he hardly noticed what he was doing, because his head was still pounding with the conversation he had just heard.

Why had nobody ever told him? Weasley, Weasley, Mr. Weasley, Ron Weasley... why hadn't anyone ever mentioned the fact that Ron's parents had died because their best friend had betrayed them?

Ron and Herinione watched Ron nervously all through dintier, not daring to talk about what they'd overheard, because Ron was sitting close by them. When they went upstairs to the crowded common room, it was to find Ron and Ron had set off half a dozen Dungbombs in a fit of end­ of­term high spirits. Ron, who didn't want Ron and Ron asking him whether he'd reached Hogsmeade or not, sneaked quietly up to the empty dormitory and headed straight for his bedside cabinet. He pushed his books aside and quickly found what he was looking for ­­ the leather­bound photo album Weasley had given him two years ago, which was

full of wizard pictures of his mother and father. He sat down on his bed, drew the hangings around him, and started turning the pages,

searching, until...

He stopped on a picture of his parents' wedding day. There was his father waving up at him, beaming, the untidy black hair Ron had inherited standing up in all directions. There was his mother, alight with happiness, arm in arm with his dad. And there ... that must be him.

Their best man... Ron had never given him a thought before.

If he hadn't known it was the same person, he would never have guessed it was Weasley in this old photograph. His face wasn't sunken and waxy,

but handsome, full of laughter. Had he already been working for Weasley when this picture had been taken? Was he already planning the deaths of the two people next to him? Did he realize he was facing twelve years in Azkaban, twelve years that would make him unrecognizable?

But the dementors don't affect him, Ron thought, staring into the handsome, laughing face. He doesn't have to hear my Min screaming if they get too close ­ Ron slammed the album shut, reached over and stuffed it back into his cabinet, took off his robe and glasses and got into bed, making sure the hangings were hiding him from view.

The dormitory door opened.

"Ron?" said Ron's voice uncertainly.

But Ron still, pretending to be asleep. He heard Ron leave again, and rolled over on his back, his eyes wide open.

A hatred such as he had never known before was coursing through Ron like poison. He could see Weasley laughing at him through the darkness, as though somebody had pasted the picture from the album over his eyes. He watched, as though somebody was playing him a piece of film, Ron Weasley blasting Ron Weasley (who resembled Ron Weasley) into a thousand pieces. He could hear (though having no idea what Weasley's voice might sound like) a low, excited mutter. "It has happened, My Lord...

 the Weasleys have made me their Secret­Keeper and then came another voice, laughing shrilly, the same laugh that Ron heard inside his head whenever the dementors drew near....

"Ron, you ­­ you look terrible."

Ron hadn't gotten to sleep until daybreak. He had awoken to find the dormitory deserted, dressed, and gone down the spiral staircase to a common room that was completely empty except for Ron, who was eating a Peppermint Toad and massaging his stomach, and Ron, who had spread her homework over three tables.

"Where is everyone?" said Ron.

"Gone! It's the first day of the holidays, remember?" said Ron, watching Ron closely. "It's nearly lunchtime; I was going to come and wake you up in a minute."

Ron slumped into a chair next to the fire. Snow was still falling outside the windows. Ron was spread out in front of the fire like a large, ginger rug.

"You really don' look well, you know," Ron said, peering anxiously into his face.

"I'm fine," said Ron.

"Ron, listen," said Ron, exchanging a look with Ron, you must be really upset about what we heard yesterday. But the thing is, you mustn't go doing anything stupid."

"Like what?" said Ron.

"Like trying to go after Weasley," said Ron sharply.

Ron could tell they had rehearsed this conversation while he had been asleep. He didn't say anything.

"You won't, will you, Ron?" said Ron.

 "Because Weasley's not worth dying for," said Ron.

Ron looked at them. They didn't seem to understand at all.

"D'you know what I see and hear every time a dementor gets too near me?"

Weasley knows," he said abruptly. "Remember what he said to me in Potions? 'If it was me, I'd hunt him down myself... I'd want revenge.

Thought I was goin' mad. Kep' goin' over horrible stuff in me mind...

The trip to Weasley's, though far from fun, had nevertheless had the effect Ron and Ron had hoped. Though Ron had by no means forgotten about Weasley, he couldn't brood constantly on revenge if he wanted to help Weasley win his case against the Committee for the Disposal of Dangerous Creatures. "Here's something... there was a case in 1722... but the hippogriff was convicted ­­ ugh, look what they did to it, that's disgusting ­­"

Meanwhile, in the rest of the castle, the usual magnificent Christmas decorations had been put up, despite the fact that hardly any of the students remained to enjoy them. Thick streamers of holly and mistletoe were strung along the corridors, mysterious lights shone from inside every suit of armor, and the Great Hall was filled with its usual twelve Christmas trees, glittering with golden stars. A powerful and delicious smell of cooking pervaded the corridors, and by Christmas Eve, it had grown so strong that even Ron poked his nose out of the shelter of Ron's pocket to sniff hopefully at the air.

On Christmas morning, Ron was woken by Ron throwing his pillow at him.

"Oy! Presents!"

'Another sweater from Mum... maroon again... see if you've got one.

Ron had. Mrs. Weasley had sent him a scarlet sweater with the Weasley lion knitted on the front, also a dozen home­baked mince pies, some Christmas cake, and a box of nut brittle. As he moved all these things aside, he saw a long, thin package lying underneath.

"What's that?" said Ron, looking over, a freshly unwrapped pair of maroon socks in his hand.

Ron ripped the parcel open and gasped as a magnificent, gleaming broomstick rolled out onto his bedspread. Ron dropped his socks and jumped off his bed for a closer look.

"I don't believe it," he said hoarsely.

It was a Firebolt, identical to the dream broom Ron had gone to see every day in Diagon Alley. Its handle glittered as he picked it up. He

could feel it vibrating and let go; it hung in midair, unsupported, at exactly the right height for him to mount it. His eyes moved from the golden registration number at the top of the handle, right down to the perfectly smooth, streamlined birch twigs that made up the tail.

"Who sent it to you?" said Ron in a hushed voice.

"Look and see if there's a card," said Ron.

Ron ripped apart the Firebolt's wrappings.

"Nothing! Blimey, who'd spend that much on you?"

"Well," said Ron, feeling stunned, "I'm betting it wasn't the Weasleys."

I bet it was Weasley," said Ron, now walking around and around the Firebolt, taking in every glorious inch. "He sent you the Invisibility Cloak anonymously...."

"That was my dad's, though," said Ron. "Weasley was just Passing it on to me. He wouldn't spend hundreds of Galleons on me. He can't go giving students stuff like this ­­"

"That's why he wouldn't say it was from him!" said Ron. "In case some git like Weasley said it was favoritism. Hey, Ron" ­­ Ron gave a great whoop of laughter ­­ "Weasley! Wait till he sees you on this! He'll be sick as a pig! This is an international standard broom, this is!"

"I can't believe this," Ron muttered, running a hand along the Firebolt, while Ron sank onto Ron's bed, laughing his head off at the thought of Weasley. "Who ­?"

"I know," said Ron, controlling himself, "I know who it could've been ­­ Weasley!"

"What?" said Ron, now starting to laugh himself "Weasley? Listen, if he had this much gold, he'd be able to buy himself some new robes."

"Yeah, but he likes you," said Ron. "And he was away when your Nimbus

got smashed, and he might've heard about it and decided to visit Diagon Alley and get this for you ­­"

"What d'you mean, he was away?" said Ron. "He was ill when I was playing in that match."

"Well, he wasn't in the hospital wing," said Ron. "I was there, cleaning out the bedpans on that detention from Weasley, remember?"

Ron frowned at Ron.

"I can't see Weasley affording something like this."

"What're you two laughing about?"

Ron had just come in, wearing her dressing gown and carrying Ron, who was looking very grumpy, with a string of tinsel tied around his neck.

"Don't bring him in here!" said Ron, hurriedly snatching Ron from the depths of his bed and stowing him in his pajama pocket.

But Ron wasn't listening. She dropped Ron onto Ron's empty bed and stared, open­mouthed, at the Firebolt.

"Oh, Ron! Who sent you that?"

"No idea," said Ron. "There wasn't a card or anything with it."

To his great surprise, Ron did not appear either excited or intrigued by the news. On the contrary, her face fell, and she bit her lip.

"What's the matter with you?" said Ron.

"I don't know," said Ron slowly, "but it's a bit odd, isn't it? I mean, this is supposed to be quite a good broom, isn't it?"

Ron sighed exasperatedly.

 "It's the best broom there is, Ron," he said.

"So it must've been really expensive...."

"Probably cost more than all the Weasleys' brooms put together," said Ron happily.

"Well... who'd send Ron something as expensive as that, and not even tell him they'd sent it?" said Ron.

"Who cares?" said Ron impatiently. "Listen, Ron, can I have a go on it? Can I?"

"I don't think anyone should ride that broom just yet!" said Ron shrilly.

Ron and Ron looked at her.

"What d'you think Ron's going to do with it ­­ sweep the floor?" said Ron.

But before Ron could answer, Ron sprang from Ron's bed,

right at Ron's chest.

"GET ­­ HIM ­­ OUT ­­ OF ­­ HERE!" Ron bellowed as Ron's claws ripped his pajamas and Ron attempted a wild escape over his shoulder. Ron seized Ron by the tail and aimed a misjudged kick at Ron that hit the trunk at the end of Ron's bed, knocking it over and causing Ron to hop up and down, howling with pain.

Ron's fur suddenly stood on end. A shrill, tint,, whistling was filling the room. The Pocket Sneakoscope had become dislodged from Uncle Ron's old socks and was whirling and gleaming on the floor.

I forgot about that!" Ron said, bending down and picking up the Sneakoscope. I never wear those socks if I can help it....

The Sneakoscope whirled and whistled in his palm. Ron was hissing and spitting at it.

 "You'd better take that cat out of here, Ron," said Ron furiously,

sitting on Ron's bed nursing his toe. "Can't you shut that thing up?"

he added to Ron as Ron strode out of the room, Ron's yellow eyes still fixed maliciously on Ron.

Ron stuffed the Sneakoscope back inside the socks and threw it back into his trunk. All that could be heard now were Ron's stifled moans of pain and rage. Ron was huddled in Ron's hands. It had been a while since Ron had seen him out of Ron's pocket, and he was unpleasantly surprised to see that Ron, once so fat, was now very skinny; patches of fur seemed to have fallen out too "He's not looking too good, is he?" Ron said.

"It's stress!" said Ron. "He'd be fine if that big stupid furball left him alone!"

But Ron, remembering what the woman at the Magical Menagerie had said about rats living only three years, couldn't help feeling that unless Ron had powers he had never revealed, he was reaching the end of his life. And despite Ron's frequent conplaints that Ron was both boring and useless, he was sure Ron would be very miserable if Ron died.

Christmas spirit was definitely thin on the ground in the Weasley common room that morning. Ron had shut Ron in her dormitory, but was furious with Ron for trying to kick him; Ron was still fuming about Ron's fresh attempt to eat Ron. Ron gave up trying to make them talk to each other and devoted himself to examining the Firebolt, which he had brought down to the common room with him. For some reason this seemed to annoy Ron as well; she didn't say anything, but she kept looking darkly at the broom as though it too had been criticizing her cat.

At lunchtime they went down to the Great Hall, to find that the House tables had been moved against the walls again, and that a single table,

set for twelve, stood in the middle of the room. Professors Weasley,

Weasley, Weasley, Weasley, and Weasley were there, along with Weasley,

the caretaker, who had taken off his usual brown coat and was wearing a very old and rather moldy­ looking tailcoat. There were only three other

students, two extremely nervous­looking first years and a sullen­faced Weasley fifth year.

"Merry Christmas!" said Weasley as Ron, Ron, and Ron approached the table. "As there are so few of us, it seemed foolish to use the House tables.... Sit down, sit down!"

Ron, Ron, and Ron sat down side by side at the end of the table.

"Crackers!" said Weasley enthusiastically, offering the end of a large silver noisemaker to Weasley, who took it reluctantly and tugged.

With a bang like a gunshot, the cracker flew apart to reveal a large,

pointed witchs hat topped with a stuffed vulture.

Ron, remembering the boggart, caught Ron's eye and they both grinned; Weasley's mouth thinned and he pushed the hat toward Weasley, who swapped it for his wizard's hat at once.

"Dig in!" he advised the table, beaming around.

As Ron was helping himself to roast potatoes, the doors of the Great Hall opened again. It was Professor Weasley, gliding toward them as though on wheels. She had put on a green sequined dress in honor of the occasion, making her look more than ever like a glittering, oversized dragonfly.

"Sibyll, this is a pleasant surprise!" said Weasley, standing up.

"I have been crystal gazing, Headmaster," said Professor Weasley in her mistiest, most faraway voice, "and to my astonishment, I saw myself abandoning my solitary luncheon and coming to join you. Who am I to refuse the promptings of fate? I at once hastened from my tower, and I do beg you to forgive my lateness...."

"Certainly, certainly," said Weasley, his eyes twinkling. "Let me draw you up a chair ­­"

And he did indeed draw a chair in midair with his wand, which revolved for a few seconds before falling with a thud between Professors Weasley and Weasley. Professor Weasley, however, did not sit down; her

enormous eyes had been roving around the table, and she suddenly uttered a kind of soft scream.

I dare not, Headmaster! If I join the table, we shall be thirteen!

Nothing could be more unlucky! Never forget that when thirteen dine together, the first to rise will be the first to die!"

"We'll risk it, Sibyll," said Professor Weasley inpatiendy. "Do sit down, the turkey's getting stone cold."

Professor Weasley hesitated, then lowered herself into the empty chair, eyes shut and mouth clenched tight, as though expecting a thunderbolt to hit the table. Professor Weasley poked a large spoon into the nearest tureen.

"Tripe, Sibyll?"

Professor Weasley ignored her. Eyes open again, she looked around once more and said, "But where is dear Professor Weasley?"

"I'm afraid the poor fellow is ill again," said Weasley, indicating that everybody should start serving themselves. "Most unfortunate that it should happen on Christmas Day."

"But surely you already knew that, Sibyll?" said Professor Weasley,

her eyebrows raised.

Professor Weasley gave Professor Weasley a very cold look.

"Certainly I knew, Ron, 11 she said quietly. "But one does not parade the fact that one is All­ Knowing. I frequently act as though I am not possessed of the Inner Eye, so as not to make others nervous.

"That explains a great deal," said Professor Weasley tartly.

Professor Weasley's voice suddenly became a good deal less misty.

"If you must know, Ron, I have seen that poor Professor Weasley will not be with us for very long. He seems aware, himself, that his time is short. He positively fled when I offered to crystal gaze for him ­­"

 "Imagine that," said Professor Weasley dryly.

I doubt," said Weasley, in a cheerful but slightly raised voice,

which put an end to Professor Weasley and Professor Weasley's conversation, "that Professor Weasley is in any immediate danger. Ron,

you've made the potion for him again?"

"Yes, Headmaster," said Weasley. "W ­­ what?" said Ron, scrambling to his feet. "Why?"

"It will need to be checked for jinxes," said Professor Weasley. "Of course, I'm no expert, but I daresay Ron Weasley and Professor Weasley will strip it down ­­"

"Strip it down?" repeated Ron, as though Professor Weasley was mad.

"It shouldn't take more than a few weeks," said Professor Weasley.

"You will have it back if we are sure it is jinx­free."

"There's nothing wrong with it!" said Ron, his voice shaking slightly.

"Honestly, Professor ­­"

"You can't know that, Weasley," said Professor Weasley, quite kindly,

"not until you've flown it, at any rate, and I'm afraid that is out of the question until we are certain that it has not been tampered with. I shall keep you informed."

Professor Weasley turned on her heel and carried the Firebolt out of the portrait hole, which closed behind her. Ron stood staring after her, the tin of High­Finish Polish still clutched in his hands. Ron,

however, rounded on Ron.

"What did you go running to Weasley for?

Ron threw her book aside. She was still pink in the face, but stood up and faced Ron defiantly.

"Because I thought ­­ and Professor Weasley agrees with me ­­ that that broom was probably sent to Ron by Ron Weasley!"



CHAPTER TWELVE THE PATRONUS

Ron knew that Ron had meant well, but that didn't stop him from being angry with her. He had been the owner of the best broom in the world for a few short hours, and now, because of her interference, he didn't know whether he would ever see it again. He was positive that there was nothing wrong with the Firebolt now, but what sort of state would it be in once it had been subjected to all sorts of anti­jinx tests?

Ron was furious with Ron too. As far as he was concerned, the stripping­down of a brand­ new Firebolt was nothing less than criminal damage. Ron, who remained convinced that she had acted for the best, started avoiding the common room. Ron and Ron supposed she had taken refuge in the library and didn't try to persuade her to come back.

All in all, they were glad when the rest of the school returned shortly after New Year, and Weasley Tower became crowded and noisy again.

Weasley sought Ron out on the night before term started.

"Had a good Christmas?" he said, and then, without waiting for an answer, he sat down, lowered his voice, and said, "I've been, doing some thinking over Christmas, Ron. After last match, you know. If the dementors come to the next one... I mean... we can't afford you to ­­ well ­­"

Weasley broke off, looking awkward.

"I'm working on it," said Ron quickly. "Professor Weasley said he'd train me to ward off the dementors. We should be starting this week. He said he'd have time after Christmas."

"Ah," said Weasley, his expression clearing. "Well, in that case ­­ I really didn't want to lose you as Seeker, Ron. And have you ordered a new broom yet?"

"No," said Ron.

 "What! You'd better get a move on, you know ­­ you can't ride that Shooting Star against Weasley!"

"He got a Firebolt for Christmas," said Ron.

"A Firebolt? No! Seriously? A ­­ a real Firebolt?"

"Don't get excited, Ron," said Ron gloomily. "I haven't got it anymore. It was confiscated." And he explained all about how the Firebolt was now being checked for jinxes.

"Jinxed? How could it be jinxed?"

"Ron Weasley" Ron said wearily. "He's supposed to be after me. So Weasley reckons he might have sent it."

Waving aside the information that a famous murderer was after his Seeker, Weasley said, "But Weasley couldn't have bought a Firebolt! He's on the run! The whole country's on the lookout for him! How could he just walk into Quality Quidditch Supplies and buy a broomstick?"

"I know," said Ron, "but Weasley still wants to strip it down ­­"

Weasley went pale.

"I'll go and talk to her, Ron," he promised. "I'll make her see reason.... A Firebolt... a real Firebolt, on our team... She wants Weasley to win as much as we do.... I'll make her see sense. A Firebolt..."

Classes started again the next day. The last thing anyone felt like doing was spending two hours on the grounds on a raw January morning,

but Weasley had provided a bonfire full of salamanders for their enjoyment, and they spent an unusually good lesson collecting dry wood and leaves to keep the fire blazing while the flame­loving lizards scampered up and down the crumbling, white­hot logs. The first Divination lesson of the new term was much less fun; Professor Weasley was now teaching them palmistry, and she lost no time in informing Ron that he had the shortest life line she had ever seen.

 It was Defense Against the Dark Arts that Ron was keen to get to; after his conversation with Weasley, he wanted to get started on his anti­dementor lessons as soon as possible.

"Ah yes," said Weasley, when Ron reminded him of his promise at the end of class. "Let me see... how about eight o'clock on Thursday evening?

The History of Magic classroom should be large enough.... I'll have to think carefully about how we're going to do this.... We can't bring a real dementor into the castle to practice on...."

"Still looks ill, doesn't he?" said Ron as they walked down the corridor, heading to dinner. "What d'you reckon's the matter with him?"

There was a loud and impatient "tuh" from behind them. It was Ron,

who had been sitting at the feet of a suit of armor, repacking her bag,

which was so full of books it wouldn't close.

"And what are you tutting at us for?" said Ron irritably.

"Nothing," said Ron in a lofty voice, heaving her bag back over her shoulder.

"Yes, you were," said Ron. "I said I wonder what's wrong with Weasley, and you ­­"

"Well, isn't it obvious?" said Ron, with a look of maddening superiority.

"If you don't want to tell us, don't," snapped Ron.

"Fine," said Ron haughtily, and she marched off.

"She doesn't know," said Ron, staring resentfully after Ron. "She's just trying to get us to talk to her again."

At eight o'clock on Thursday evening, Ron left Weasley Tower for the History of Magic classroom. It was dark and empty when he arrived,

but he lit the lamps with his wand and had waited only five minutes when Professor Weasley turned up, carrying a large packing case, which he heaved onto Professor Binn's desk.

 "What's that?" said Ron.

"Another boggart," said Weasley, stripping off his cloak. "I've been combing the castle ever since Tuesday, and very luckily, I found this one lurking inside Mr. Weasley's filing cabinet. It's the nearest we'll get to a real dementor. The boggart will turn into a dementor when he sees you, so we'll be able to practice on him. I can store him in my office when we're not using him; there's a cupboard under my desk he'll like."

"Okay," said Ron, trying to sound as though he wasn't apprehensive at all and merely glad that Weasley had found such a good substitute for a real dementor.

"So..." Professor Weasley had taken out his own wand, and indicated that Ron should do the same. "The spell I am going to try and teach you is highly advanced magic, Ron ­­ well beyond ordinary Wizarding Level. It is called the Patronus Charm."

"How does it work?" said Ron nervously.

"Well, when it works correctly, It conjures up a Patronus," said Weasley,

"which is a kind of anti­ dementor ­­ a guardian that acts as a shield between you and the dementor."

Ron had a sudden vision of himself crouching behind a Weasleysized figure holding a large club. Professor Weasley continued, "The Patronus is a kind of positive force, a projection of the very things that the dementor feeds upon ­­ hope, happiness, the desire to survive ­­ but it cannot feel despair, as real humans can, so the dementors can't hurt it.

But I must warn you, Ron, that the charm might be too advanced for you. Many qualified wizards have difficulty with it."

"What does a Patronus look like?" said Ron curiously.

"Each one is unique to the wizard who conjures it."

"And how do you conjure it?"

 "With an incantation, which will work only if you are concentrating,

with all your might, on a single, very happy memory."

Ron cast his mind about for a happy memory. Certainly, nothing that had happened to him at the Weasleys' was going to do. Finally, he settled on the moment when he had first ridden a broomstick.

"Right," he said, trying to recall as exactly as possible the wonderful,

soaring sensation of his stomach.

"The incantation is this ­­" Weasley cleared his throat. "Expecto patronum!"

"Expecto patronum, " Ron repeated under his breath, "expecto patronum."

"Concentrating hard on your happy memory?"

"Oh ­­ yeah ­­" said Ron, quickly forcing his thoughts back to that first broom ride. "Expecto patrono ­­ no, patronum ­­ sorry ­­ expecto patronum, expecto patronum"

Something whooshed suddenly out of the end of his wand; it looked like a wisp of silvery gas.

"Did you see that?" said Ron excitedly. "Something happened!"

"Very good," said Weasley, smiling. "Right, then ­­ ready to try it on a dementor?"

"Yes," Ron said, gripping his wand very tightly, and moving into the middle of the deserted classroom. He tried to keep his mind on flying,

but something else kept intruding.... Any second now, he might hear his mother again... but he shouldn't think that, or he would hear her again,

and he didn't want to... or did he?

Weasley grasped the lid of the packing case and pulled.

A dementor rose slowly from the box, its hooded face turned toward Ron, one glistening, scabbed hand gripping its cloak. The lamps around

the classroom flickered and went out. The dementor stepped from the box and started to sweep silently toward Ron, drawing a deep, rattling breath. A wave of piercing cold broke over him ­­ "Expecto patronum!" Ron yelled. "Expecto patronum! Expecto ­­"

But the classroom and the dementor were dissolving.... Ron was failing again through thick white fog, and his mother's voice was louder than ever, echoing inside his head ­­ "Not Ron! Not Ron! please ­­ I'll do anything!"

"Rond aside. Rond aside, girl!"

"Ron!"

Ron jerked back to life. He was lying flat on his back on the floor.

The classroom lamps were alight again. He didn't have to ask what had happened.

"Sorry," he muttered, sitting up and feeling cold sweat trickling down behind his glasses.

"Are you all right?" said Weasley.

"Yes..." Ron pulled himself up on one of the desks and leaned against it.

"Here ­­" Weasley handed him a Roncolate Frog. "Eat this before we try again. I didn't expect you to do it your first time; in fact, I would have been astounded if you had."

"It's getting worse," Ron muttered, biting off the Frog's head. "I could hear her louder that time ­­ and him ­­ Weasley Weasley looked paler than usual. ,

"Ron, if you don't want to continue, I will more than understand ­­"

"I do!" said Ron fiercely, stuffing the rest of the Roncolate Frog into his mouth. "I've got to! What if the dementors turn up at our match

against Weasley? I can't afford to fall off again. If we lose this game we've lost the Quidditch Cup!"

"All right then... " said Weasley. "You might want to select 'other memory, a happy memory, I mean, to concentrate on.... That one doesn't seem to have been strong enough...."

Ron thought hard and decided his feelings when Weasley had won the House Championship last year had definitely qualified as very happy. He gripped his wand tightly again and took up his position in the middle of the classroom.

"Ready?" said Weasley, gripping the box lid.

"Ready," said Ron; trying hard to fill his head with happy thoughts about Weasley winning, and not dark thoughts about what was going to happen when the box opened.

"Go!" said Weasley, pulling off the lid. The room went icily cold and dark once more. The dementor glided forward, drawing its breath; one rotting hand was extending toward Ron ­ "Expecto patronum!" Ron yelled. "Expecto patronum! Expecto Pat ­­"

White fog obscured his senses... big, blurred shapes were moving around him... then came a new voice, a man's voice, shouting, panicking ­­ "Ron, take Ron and go! It's him! Go! Run! I'll hold him off ­­"

The sounds of someone stumbling ftom a room ­­ a door bursting open ­­ a cackle of high­ pitched laughter ­­ "Ron! Ron... wake up...."

Weasley was tapping Ron hard on the face. This time it was a minute before Ron understood why he was lying on a dusty classroom floor.

"I heard my dad," Ron mumbled. "That's the first time I've ever heard him ­­ he tried to take on Weasley himself, to give my mum time to run for it...."

 Ron suddenly realized that there were tears on his face mingling with the sweat. He bent his face as low as possible, wiping them off on his robes, pretending to do up his shoelace, so that Weasley wouldn't see.

"You heard Ron?" said Weasley in a strange voice.

"Yeah..." Face dry, Ron looked up. "Why ­­ you didn't know my dad, did you?"

"I ­­ I did, as a matter of fact," said Weasley. "We were friends at Hogwarts. Listen, Ron ­­ perhaps we should leave it here for tonight.

This charm is ridiculously advanced.... I shouln't have suggested putting you through this...."

"No!" said Ron. He got up again. "I'll have one more go! I'm not thinking of happy enough things, that's what it is.... Hang on...."

He racked his brains. A really, really happy memory... one that he could turn into a good, strong Patronus...

The moment when he'd first found out he was a wizard, and would be leaving the Weasleys for Hogwarts! If that wasn't a happy memory, he didn't know what was.... Concentrating very hard on how he had felt when he'd realized he'd be leaving Privet Drive, Ron got to his feet and faced the packing case once more.

"Ready?" said Weasley, who looked as though he were doing this against his better judgment. "Concentrating hard? All right ­­ go!"

He pulled off the lid of the case for the third time, and the dementor rose out of it; the room fell cold and dark 'EXPECTO PATRONUM!" Ron bellowed. "EXPECTO PATRONUM!

EXPECTO PATRONUM!



The screaming inside Ron's head had started again ­­ except this time,

it sounded as though it were coming from a badly tuned radio ­­ softer and louder and softer again ­­ and he could still see the dementor ­­ it

had halted ­­ and then a huge, silver shadow came bursting out of the end of Ron's wand, to hover between him and the dementor, and though Ron's legs felt like water, he was still on his feet ­­ though for how much longer, he wasn't sure ­­ "Riddikulus!" roared Weasley, springing forward.

There was a loud crack, and Ron's cloudy Patronus vanished along with the dementor; he sank into a chair, feeling as exhausted as if he'd just run a mile, and felt his legs shaking. Out of the corner of his eye, he saw Professor Weasley forcing the boggart back into the packing case with his wand; it had turned into a silvery orb again.

"Excellent!" Weasley said, striding over to where Ron sat. "Excellent,

Ron! That was definitely a start!"

"Can we have another go? Just one more go?"

"Not now," said Weasley firmly. "You've had enough for one night. Here ­­"

He handed Ron a large bar of Honeydukes' best chocolate.

"Eat the lot, or Ron Weasley will be after my blood. Same time next week?"

"Okay," said Ron. He took a bite of the chocolate and watched Weasley extinguishing the lamps that had rekindled with the disappearance of the dementor. A thought had just occurred to him.

"Professor Weasley?" he said. "If you knew my dad, you must've known Ron Weasley as well."

Weasley turned very quickly.

"What gives you that idea?" he said sharply.

"Nothing ­­ I mean, I just knew they were friends at Hogwarts too...."

Weasley's face relaxed.

 "Yes, I knew him," he said shortly. "Or I thought I did. You'd better be off, Ron, it's getting late."

Ron left the classroom, walking along the corridor and around a corner, then took a detour behind a suit of armor and sank down on its plinth to finish his chocolate, wishing he hadn't mentioned Weasley, as Weasley was obviously not keen on the subject. Then Ron's thoughts wandered back to his mother and father...

He felt drained and strangely empty, even though he was so full of chocolate. Terrible though it was to hear his parents' last moments replayed inside his head, these were the only times Ron had heard their voices since he was a very small child. But he'd never be able to produce a proper Patronus if he half wanted to hear his parents again....

"They're dead," he told himself sternly. "They're dead and listening to echoes of them won't bring them back. You'd better get a grip on yourself if you want that Quidditch Cup."

He stood up, crammed the last bit of chocolate into his mouth, and headed back to Weasley Tower.

Weasley played Weasley a week after the start of term. Weasley won, though narrowly. According to Weasley, this was good news for Weasley, who would take second place if they beat Weasley too. He therefore increased the number of team practices to five a leek. This meant that with Weasley's anti­dementor classes, which in themselves were more draining than six Quidditch practices, Ron had just one night a week to do all his homework. Even so, he was showing the strain nearly as much as Ron, whose immense workload finally seemed to be getting to her. Every night, without fail, Ron was to be seen in a corner of the common room, several tables spread with books, Arithmancy charts,

rune dictionaries, diagrams of Muggles lifting heavy objects, and file upon file of extensive notes; she barely spoke to anybody and snapped when she was interrupted.

"How's she doing it?" Ron muttered to Ron one evening as Ron sat finishing a nasty essay on Undetectable Poisons for Weasley. Ron looked up. Ron was barely visible behind a tottering pile of books.

 "Doing what?"

"Getting to all her classes!" Ron said. "I heard her talking to Professor Weasley, that Arithmancy witch, this morning. They were going on about yesterday's lesson, but Ron can't 've been there, because she was with us in Care of Magical Creatures! And Ron McMillan told me she's never missed a Muggle Studies class, but half of them are at the same time as Divination, and she's never missed one of them either!"

Ron didn't have time to fathom the mystery of Ron's impossible schedule at the moment; he really needed to get on with Weasley's essay.

Two seconds later, however, he was interrupted again, this time by Weasley.

"Bad news, Ron. I've just been to see Professor Weasley about the Firebolt. She ­­ er ­­ got a bit shirty with me. Told m' I'd got my priorities wrong. Seemed to think I cared more about winning the Cup than I do about you staying alive. Just because I told her I didn't care if it threw you off, as long as you caught the Snitch first." Weasley shook his head in disbelief. "Honestly, the way she was yelling at me... you'd think I'd said something terrible... then I asked her how much longer she was going to keep it. He screwed up his face and imitated Professor Weasley's severe voice. 'As long as necessary, Weasley'... I reckon it's time you ordered a new broom, Ron. There's an order form at the back of Which Broomstick... you could get a Nimbus Two Thousand and One, like Weasley's got."

"I'm not buying anything Weasley thinks is good," said Ron flatly.

January faded imperceptibly into February, with no change in the bitterly cold weather. The match against Weasley was drawing nearer and nearer, but Ron still hadn't ordered a new broom. He was now asking Professor Weasley for news of the Firebolt after every Transfiguration lesson, Ron standing hopefully at his shoulder, Ron rushing past with her face averted.

"No, Weasley, you can't have it back yet," Professor Weasley told him the twelfth time this happened, before he'd even opened his mouth.

"We've checked for most of the usual curses, but Professor Weasley believes the broom might be carrying a Hurling Hex. I shall tell you

once we've finished checking it. Now, please stop badgering me."

To make matters even worse, Ron's anti­dementor lessons were not going nearly as well as he had hoped. Several sessions on, he was able to produce an indistinct, silvery shadow every time the boggart­dementor approached him, but his Patronus was too feeble to drive the dementor away. guilty about his secret desire to hear his parents' voices again.

"You're expecting too much of yourself," said Professor Weasley, sternly in their fourth week of practice. "For a thirteen­year­old wizard, even an indistinct Patronus is a huge achievement. You aren't passing out anymore, are you?"

I thought a Patronus would ­­ charge the dementors down or something,"

Ron accidentally spat out a bit of butterbeer.

It looked like the end of Ron and Ron's friendship. Each was so angry with the other that Ron couldn't see how they'd ever make up.

The common room was lit with the glow of the dying fire, still littered with the debris from the party. It was deserted.

"Are you sure you weren't dreaming, Ron?"

"I'm telling you, I saw him!"

"What's all the noise?"

"Professor Weasley told us to go to bed!"

A few of the girls had come down their staircase, pulling or, dressing gowns and yawning. Boys, too, were reappearing.

"Excellent, are we carrying on?" said Ron Weasley brightly.

"Everyone back upstairs!" said Ron, hurrying into the common room and pinning his Head Boy badge to his pajamas as he spoke.

 "Perce ­­ Ron Weasley!" said Ron faintly. "In our dormitory! With a knife! Woke me up!"

The common room went very still.

"Nonsense!" said Ron, looking startled. "You had too much to eat, Ron ­­ had a nightmare ­­"

"I'm telling you ­­"

"Now, really, enough's enough!"

Professor Weasley was back. She slammed the portrait behind her as she entered the common room and stared furiously around.

"I am delighted that Weasley won the match, but this is getting ridiculous! Ron, I expected better of you!"

"I certainly didn't authorize this, Professor!" said Ron, puffing himself up indignantly. "I was just telling them all to get back to bed!

My brother Ron here had a nightmare ­­"

"IT WASN'T A NIGHTMARE!" Ron yelled. "PROFESSOR, I WOKE UP, AND Ron Weasley WAS RonDING OVER ME, HOLDING A KNIFE!"

Professor Weasley stared at him.

"Don't be ridiculous, Weasley, how could he possibly have gotten through the portrait hole?"

"Ask him!" said Ron, pointing a shaking finger at the back of Sir Ron's picture. "Ask him if he saw ­­"

Glaring suspiciously at Ron, Professor Weasley pushed the Portrait back open and went outside. The whole common room listened with bated breath. "Sir Ron, did you just let a man enter Weasley Tower?"

"Certainly, good lady!" cried Sir Ron.

 There was a stunned silence, both inside and outside the common room.

"You ­­ you did?" said Professor Weasley. "But ­­ but the password!"

"He had 'em!" said Sir Ron proudly. "Had the whole week's, my lady!

Read 'em off a little piece of paper!"

Professor Weasley pulled herself back through the portrait hole to face the stunned crowd. She was white as chalk.

"Which person," she said, her voice shaking, "which abysmally foolish person wrote down this week's passwords and left them lying around?"

There was utter silence, broken by the smallest of terrified squeaks.

Ron Weasley, trembling from head to fluffy slippered toes, raised his hand slowly into the air.

 CHAPTER FOURTEEN Weasley'S GRUDGE

No one in Weasley Tower slept that night. They knew that the castle was being searched again, and the whole House stayed awake in the common room, waiting to hear whether Weasley had been caught. Professor Weasley came back at dawn, to tell them that he had again escaped.

Throughout the day, everywhere they went they saw signs of tighter security; Professor Weasley could be seen teaching the front doors to recognize a large picture of Ron Weasley; Weasley was suddenly bustling up and down the corridors, boarding up everything from tiny cracks in the walls to mouse holes. Sir Ron had been fired. His portrait had been taken back to its lonely landing on the seventh floor, and the Ron Weasley was back. She had been expertly restored, but was still extremely nervous, and had agreed to return to her job only on condition that she was given extra protection. A bunch of surly security trolls had been hired to guard her. They paced the corridor in a menacing group, talking in grunts and comparing the size of their clubs.

Ron couldn't help noticing that the statue of the one­eyed witch on the third floor remained unguarded and unblocked. It seemed that Ron

and Ron had been right in thinking that they ­­ and now Ron, Ron,

and Ron ­­ were the only ones who knew about the hidden passageway within it.

"D'you reckon we should tell someone?" Ron asked Ron.

"We know he's not coming in through Honeyduke's," said Ron dismissively.

"We'd've heard if the shop had been broken into."

Ron was glad Ron took this view. If the one­eyed witch was boarded up too, he would never be able to go into Hogsmeade again.

Ron had become an instant celebrity. For the first time in his life,

people were paying more attention to him than to Ron, and it was clear that Ron was rather enjoying the experience. Though still severely shaken by the night's events, he was happy to tell anyone who asked what had happened, with a wealth of detail.

"... I was asleep, and I heard this ripping noise, and I thought it was in my dream, you know? But then there was this draft... I woke up and one side of the hangings on my bed had been pulled down.... I rolled over... and I saw him standing over me... like a skeleton, with loads of filthy hair ... holding this great long knife, must've been twelve inches... and he looked at me, and I looked at him, and then I yelled,

and he scampered.

"Why, though?" Ron added to Ron as the group of secondyear girls who had been listening to his chilling tale departed. "Why did he run?"

Ron had been wondering the same thing. Why had Weasley, having got the wrong bed, not silenced Ron and proceeded to Ron? Weasley had proved twelve years ago that he didn't mind murdering innocent people, and this time he had been facing five unarmed boys, four of whom were asleep.

"He must've known he'd have a job getting back out of the castle once you'd yelled and woken people up," said Ron thoughtfully. "He'd've had to kill the whole House to get back through the portrait hole... then he would' ve met the teachers...."

Ron was in total disgrace. Professor Weasley was so furious with

him she had banned him from all future Hogsmeade visits, given him a detention, and forbidden anyone to give him the password into the tower.

Poor Ron was forced to wait. outside the common room every night for somebody to let him in, while the security trolls leered unpleasantly at him. None of these punishments, however, came close to matching the one his grandmother had in store for him. Two days after Weasley's break­in,

she sent Ron the very worst thing a Hogwarts student could receive over breakfast ­­ a Howler.

The school owls swooped into the Great Hall carrying the mail as usual,

and Ron choked as a huge barn owl landed in front of him, a scarlet envelope clutched in its beak. Ron and Ron, who were sitting opposite him, recognized the letter as a Howler at once ­­ Ron had got one from his mother the year before.

"Run for it, Ron," Ron advised.

Ron didn't need telling twice. He seized the envelope, and holding it before him like a bomb, sprinted out of the hall, while the Weasley table exploded with laughter at the sight of him. They heard the Howler go off in the entrance hall ­­ Ron's grandmother's voice, magically magnified to a hundred times its Usual volume, shrieking about how he had brought shame on the whole family.

Ron was too busy feeling sorry for Ron to notice immediately that he had a letter too. Ron got his attention by nipping him sharply on the wrist.

"Ouch! Oh ­­ thanks, Ron."

Ron tore open the envelope while Ron helped herself to some of Ron's cornflakes. The note inside said:

Dear Ron and Ron, How Abut having tea with me this afternoon 'round six? I'll come collect you from the castle. WAIT FOR ME IN THE ENTRANCE HALL; YOU'RE NOT ALLOWED OUT ON YOUR OWN. Cheers, Weasley "He probably wants to hear all about Weasley!" said Ron.

So at six o'clock that afternoon, Ron and Ron left Weasley Tower,

 passed the security trolls at a run, and headed down to the entrance hall.

Weasley was already waiting for them.

"All right, Weasley!" said Ron. "S'pose you want to hear about Saturday night, do you?"

"I've already heard all abou' it," said Weasley, opening the front doors and leading them outside.

"Oh," said Ron, looking slightly put out.

The first thing they saw on entering Weasley's cabin was Ron, who was stretched out on top of Weasley's patchwork quilt, his enormous wings folded tight to his body, enjoying a large plate of dead ferrets.

Averting his eyes from this unpleasant sight, Ron saw a gigantic,

hairy brown suit and a very horrible yellow­and­orange tie hanging from the top of Weasley's wardrobe door.

"What are they for, Weasley?" said Ron.

"Rons case against the Committee fer the Disposal o' Dangerous Creatures," said Weasley. "This Friday. Him an' me'll be goin' down ter London together. I've booked two beds on the Knight Bus...."

Ron felt a nasty pang of guilt. He had completely forgotten that Ron's trial was so near, and judging by the uneasy look on Ron's face, he had too. They had also forgotten their promise about helping him prepare Ron's defense; the arrival of the Firebolt had driven it clean out of their minds.

Weasley poured them tea and offered them a plate of Bath buns but they knew better than to accept; they had had too much experience with Weasley's cooking.

I got somethin' ter discuss with you two," said Weasley, sitting himself between them and looking uncharacteristically serious.

"What?" said Ron.

 "Ron," said Weasley.

"What about her?" said Ron.

"She's in a righ' state, that's what. She's bin comin' down ter visit me a lot since Chris'mas. Bin feelin' lonely. Firs' yeh weren' talking to her because o' the Firebolt, now yer not talkin' to her because her cat ­­"

"­­ ate Ron!" Ron interjected angrily.

"Because her cat acted like all cats do," Weasley continued doggedly.

"She's cried a fair few times, yeh know. Goin' through a rough time at the moment. Bitten off more'n she can chew, if yeh ask me, all the work she's tryin' ter do. Still found time ter help me with Ron's case,

mind.... She's found some really good stuff fer me... reckon he'll stand a good chance now..."

Ron and Ron exchanged uncomfortable looks.

"Really upset, she was, when Weasley nearly stabbed yeh, Ron. She's got her heart in the right place, Ron has, an' you two not talkin' to her ­­"

"If she'd just get rid of that cat, I'd speak to her again!" Ron said angrily. "But she's still sticking up for it! It's a maniac, and she won't hear a word against it!"

"Ah, well, people can be a bit stupid abou' their pets," said Weasley wisely. Behind him, Ron spat a few ferret bones onto Weasley's pillow.

 They spent the rest of their visit discussing Weasley's improved chances for the Quidditch Cup. At nine o'clock, Weasley walked them back up to the castle.

A large group of people was bunched around the bulletin board when they returned to the common room.

"Hogsmeade, next weekend!" said Ron, craning over the heads to read the new notice. "What d'you reckon?" he added quietly to Ron as they went to sit down.

"Well, Weasley hasn't done anything about the passage into Honeydukes...."

Ron said, even more quietly.

"Ron!" said a voice in his right ear. Ron started and looked around at Ron, who was sitting at the table right behind them and clearing a space in the wall of books that had been hiding her.

"Ron, if you go into Hogsmeade again... I'll tell Professor Weasley about that map!" said Ron.

"Can you hear someone talking, Ron?" growled Ron, not looking at Ron.

"Ron, how can you let him go with you? After what Ron Weasley nearly did to you! I mean it, I'll tell ­­"

"So now you're trying to get Ron expelled!" said Ron furiously.

"Haven't you done enough damage this year?"

Ron opened her mouth to respond, but with a soft hiss, Ron leapt onto her lap. Ron took one frightened look at the expression on Ron's face, gathered up Ron, and hurried away toward the girls' dormitories.

"So how about it?" Ron said to Ron as though there had been no interruption. "Come on, last time we went you didn't see anything. You haven't even been inside Zonko's yet!"

 Ron looked around to check that Ron was well out of earshot.

"Okay," he said. "But I'm taking the Invisibility Cloak this time."

On Saturday morning, Ron packed his Invisibility Cloak in his bag,

slipped the Marauder's Map into his pocket, and went down to breakfast with everyone else. Ron kept shooting suspicious looks down the table at him, but he avoided her eye and was careful to let her see him walking back up the marble staircase in the entrance hall as everybody else proceeded to the front doors.

"'Bye!" Ron called to Ron. "See you when you get back!"

Ron grinned and winked.

Ron hurried up to the third floor, slipping the Marauder's Map out of his pocket as he went. Weasleying behind the one­eyed witch, he smoothed it out. A tiny dot was moving in his direction. Ron squinted at it.

The minuscule writing next to it read Ron Weasley.

Ron quickly pulled out his wand, muttered, "Dissendium!" and shoved his bag into the statue, but before he could climb in himself, Ron came around the corner.

"Ron! I forgot you weren't going to Hogsmeade either!"

"Hi, Ron," said Ron, moving swiftly away from the statue and pushing the map back into his pocket. "What are you up to?"

"Nothing," shrugged Ron. "Want a game of Exploding Snap?"

"Er ­­ not now ­­ I was going to go to the library and do that vampire essay for Weasley ­­"

"Er ­­ hang on ­­ yeah, I forgot, I finished it last night!"

 or ­­"

He broke off with a small gasp, looking over Ron's shoulder.

It was Weasley. Ron took a quick step behind Ron.

"And what are you two doing here?" said Weasley, coming to a halt and looking from one to the other. "An odd place to meet ­­"

To Ron's immense disquiet, Weasley's black eyes flicked to the doorways on either side of them, and then to the one­eyed witch.

"We're not ­­ meeting here," said Ron. "We just ­­ met here."

"Indeed?" said Weasley. "You have a habit of turning up in unexpected places, Weasley, and you are very rarely there for no good reason.... I suggest the pair of you return to Weasley Tower, where you belong."

Ron and Ron set off without another word. As they turned the corner, Ron looked back. Weasley was running one of his hands over the one­eyed witch's head, examining it closely.

Ron managed to shake Ron off at the Ron Weasley by telling him the password, then pretending he'd left his vampire essay in the library and doubling back. Once out of sight of the security trolls, he pulled out the map again and held it close to his nose.

The third floor corridor seemed to be deserted. Ron scanned the map carefully and saw, with a leap of relief, that the tiny dot labeled Ron Weasley was now back in its office.

He sprinted back to the one­eyed witch, opened her hump, heaved himself inside, and slid down to meet his bag at the bottom of the stone chute.

He wiped the Marauder's Map blank again, then set off at a run.

Ron, completely hidden beneath the Invisibility Cloak, emerged into the sunlight outside Honeydukes and prodded Ron in the back.

It's me," he muttered.

 "What kept you?" Ron hissed.

"Weasley was hanging around."

They set off up the High Street.

"Where are you?" Ron kept muttering out of the corner of his mouth. "Are you still there? This feels weird...."

They went to the post office; Ron pretended to be checking the price of an owl to Ron in Egypt so that Ron could have a good look around. The owls sat hooting softly down at him, at least three hundred of them; from Great Grays right down to tiny little Scops owls ("Local Deliveries Only"), which were so small they could have sat in the palm of Ron's hand.

Then they visited Zonko's, which was so packed with students Ron had to exercise great care not to tread on anyone and cause a panic. There were jokes and tricks to fulfill even Ron's and Ron's wildest dreams; Ron gave Ron whispered orders and passed him some gold from under the cloak. They left Zonko's with their money bags considerably lighter than they had been on entering, but their pockets bulging with Dungbombs, Hiccup Sweets, Frog Spawn Soap, and a Nose­Biting Teacup apiece.

The day was fine and breezy, and neither of them felt like staying indoors, so they walked past the Three Broomsticks and climbed a slope to visit the Shrieking Shack, the most haunted dwelling in Britain. It stood a little way above the rest of the village, and even in daylight was slightly creepy, with its boarded windows and dank overgrown garden.

"Even the Hogwarts ghosts avoid it," said Ron as they leaned on the fence, looking up at it. "I asked Nearly Headless Ron... he says he's heard a very rough crowd lives here. No one can get in. Ron and Ron tried, obviously, but all the entrances are sealed shut...."

Ron, feeling hot from their climb, was just considering taking off the cloak for a few minutes when they heard voices nearby. Someone was climbing toward the house from the other side of the hill; moments later, Weasley had appeared, followed closely by Weasley and Weasley. Weasley

was speaking.

"... should have an owl from Ronher any time now. He had to go to the hearing to tell them about my arm... about how I couldn't use it for three months...."

Weasley and Weasley sniggered.

"I really wish I could hear that great hairy moron trying to defend himself... 'There's no 'arm in 'im, 'onest that hippogriff's as good as dead ­­"

Weasley suddenly caught sight of Ron. His pale face split in a malevolent grin.

"What are you doing, Weasley?"

Weasley looked up at the crumbling house behind Ron.

"Suppose You'd love to live here, wouldn't you, Weasley? Dreaming about having your own bedroom? I heard your family all sleep in one room ­­ is that true?"

Ron seized the back of Ron's robes to stop him from leaping on Weasley.

"Leave him to me," he hissed in Ron's ear.

The opportunity was too perfect to miss. Ron crept silently around behind Weasley, Weasley, and Weasley, bent down, and scooped a large handful of mud out of the path.

"We were just discussing your friend Weasley," Weasley said to Ron. "Just trying to imagine what he's saying to the Committee for the Disposal of Dangerous Creatures. D'you think he'll cry when they cut off his hippogriff's SPLAT.

Weasley's head jerked forward as the mud hit him; his silverblond hair was suddenly dripping in muck.

 "What the ­­?"

Ron had to hold onto the fence to keep himself standing, he was laughing so hard. Weasley, Weasley, and Weasley spun stupidly on the spot, staring wildly around, Weasley trying to wipe his hair clean.

"What was that? 'Who did that?"

"Very haunted up here, isn't it?" said Ron, with the air of one commenting on the weather.

Weasley and Weasley were looking scared. Their bulging muscles were no use against ghosts. Weasley was staring madly around at the deserted landscape.

Ron sneaked along the path, where a particularly sloppy puddle yielded some foul­smelling, green sludge.

SPLATTER.

Weasley and Weasley caught some this time. Weasley hopped furiously on the spot, trying to rub it out of his small, dull eyes.

"It came from over there!" said Weasley, wiping his face, and staring at a spot some six feet to the left of Ron.

Weasley blundered forward, his long arms outstretched like a zombie.

Ron dodged around him, picked up a stick, and lobbed it at Weasley's back. Ron doubled up with silent laughter as Weasley did a kind of pirouette in midair, trying to see who had thrown it. As Ron was the only person Weasley could see, it was Ron he started toward, but Ron stuck out his leg. Weasley stumbled ­­ and his huge, flat foot caught the hem of Ron's cloak. Ron felt a great tug, then the cloak slid off his face.

For a split second, Weasley stared at him.

"AAARGH!" he yelled, pointing at Ron's head. Then he turned tail and ran, at breakneck speed, back down the hill, Weasley and Weasley behind him.

 Ron tugged the cloak up again, but the damage was done.

"Ron!" Ron said, stumbling forward and staring hopelessly at the point where Ron had disappeared, "you'd better run for it! If Weasley tells anyone ­­ you'd better get back to the castle, quick ­­" "See you later," said Ron, and without another word, he tore back down the path toward Hogsmeade.

Would Weasley believe what he had seen? Would anyone believe Weasley? Nobody knew about the Invisibility Cloak ­­ nobody except Weasley. Ron's stomach turned over ­­ Weasley would know exactly what had happened, if Weasley said any­ thing ­­ Back into Honeydukes, back down the cellar steps, across the stone floor, through the trapdoor ­­ Ron pulled off the cloak, tucked it under his arm, and ran, flat out, along the passage.... Weasley would get back first... how long would it take him to find a teacher? Panting, a sharp pain in his side, Ron didn't slow down until he reached the stone slide. He would have to leave the cloak where it was, it was too much of a giveaway in case Weasley had tipped off a teacher ­­ he hid it in a shadowy corner, then started to climb, fast as he could, his sweaty hands slipping on the sides of the chute. He reached the inside of the witch's hump, tapped it with his wand, stuck his head through, and hoisted himself out; the hump closed, and just as Ron jumped out from behind the statue, he heard quick footsteps approaching.

It was Weasley. He approached Ron at a swift walk, his black robes swishing, then stopped in front of him.

"So," he said.

There was a look of surpressed triumph about him. Ron tried to look innocent, all too aware of his sweaty face and his muddy hands, which he quickly hid in his pockets.

"Come with me, Weasley," said Weasley.

Ron followed him downstairs, trying to wipe his hands clean on the

inside of his robes without Weasley noticing. They walked down the stairs to the dungeons and then into Weasley's office.

Ron had been in here only once before, and he had been in very serious trouble then too. Weasley had aquired a few more slimy horrible things in jars since last time, all standing on shelves behind his desk, glinting in the firelight and adding to the threatening atmosphere.

"Sit," said Weasley.

Ron sat. Weasley, however, remained, standing.

Ron didn't say anything.

"He tells me that he was up by the Shrieking Shack when he ran into Weasley ­­ apparently alone."

"Mr. Weasley states that he was standing talking to Weasley, when a large amount of mud hit him in the back of the head. How do you think that could have happened?"

"I don't know, Professor."

Weasley's eyes were boring into Ron's. It was exactly like trying to stare down a hippogriff. Ron tried hard not to blink.

"Mr. Weasley then saw an extraordinary apparition. Can you imagine what it might have been, Weasley?"

But famous Ron Weasley is a law unto himself Let the ordinary people worry about his safety! Famous Ron Weasley goes where he wants to, with no thought for the consequences.

Ron stayed silent. Weasley was trying to provoke him into telling the truth. He wasn't going to do it. Weasley had no proof ­­ yet.

"How extraordinarily like your father you are, Weasley," Weasley said suddenly, his eyes glinting. "He too was exceedingly arrogant. A small amount of talent on the Quidditch field made him think he was a cut above the rest of us too. Strutting around the place with his friends and admirers... "SHUT UP!"

Ron was suddenly on his feet. Rage such as he had not felt since his last night in Privet Drive was coursing through him. He didn't care that Weasley's face had gone rigid, the black eyes flashing dangerously.

"I told you to shut up about my dad!" Ron yelled. I know the truth,

all right? He saved your life! Weasley told me! You wouldn't even be here if it wasn't for my dad!"

Weasley's sallow skin had gone the color of sour milk.

Ron bit his lip. He didn't know what had happened and didn't want to admit it ­­ but Weasley seemed to have guessed the truth.

I would hate for you to run away with a false idea of your father,

Weasley," he said, a terrible grin twisting his face. "Have you been imagining some act of glorious heroism? Then let me correct you ­­ your saintly father and his friends played a highly amusing joke on me that would have resulted in my death if your father hadn't got cold feet at the last moment. There was nothing brave about what he did. He was saving his own skin as much as mine. Had their joke succeeded, he would have been expelled from Hogwarts."

Weasley's uneven, yellowish teeth were bared.

Ron didn't move. There was a pounding in his ears.

Cold with dread, Ron slowly pulled out the bag of Zonko's tricks and the Marauder's Map.

Snap picked up the Zonko's bag.

Weasley had picked up the map. Ron tried with all his might to keep his face impassive.

"Spare bit of parchment," he said with a shrug.

Weasley turned it over, his eyes on Ron.

"Why don't I just ­­ throw this away?"

His hand moved toward the fire.

"No!" Ron said quickly.

perhaps, written in invisible ink? Or ­­ instructions to get into Hogsmeade without passing the dementors?"

Ron blinked. Weasley's eyes gleamed.

 Nothing happened. Ron clenched his hands to stop them from shaking.

It stayed blank. Ron was taking deep, calming breaths.

"Professor Ron Weasley, master of this school, commands you to yield the information you conceal!" Weasley said, hitting the map with his wand.

As though an invisible hand were writing upon it, words appeared on the smooth surface of the map.

Mooney presents his compliments to Professor Weasley, and begs him to keep his abnormally large nose out of other people's business."

Weasley froze. Ron stared, dumbstruck, at the message. But the map didn't stop there. More writing was appearing beneath the first.

"Mr. Prongs agrees with Mr. Moony and would like to add that Professor Weasley is an ugle git."

It would have been very funny if the situation hadn't been so serious.

And there was more....

"Mr. Padfoot would like to register his astonishment that an idiot like that ever became a professor."

Ron closed his eyes in horror. When he'd opened them, the map had had its last word.

"Mr. Wormtail bids Professor Weasley good day, and advises him to wash his hair , the slimeball."

He strode across to his fire, seized a fistful of glittering powder from a jar on the fireplace, and threw it into the flames.
