"Indeed?" said Weasley. His jaw had gone rigid with anger. "You think a joke shop could supply him with such a thing? You don't think it more likely that he got it directly from the manufacturers?"

Ron didn't understand what Weasley was talking about. Nor, apparently,

did Weasley.

 "You mean, by Mr. Wormtail or one of these people?" he said. "Ron, do you know any of these men?"

Right on cue, Ron came bursting into the office. He was completely out of breath, and stopped just short of Weasley's desk, clutching the stitch in his chest and trying to speak.

"I ­­ gave ­­ Ron ­­ that ­­ stuff," he choked. "Bought ­­ it... in Zonko's... ages ­­ ago..."

And I can't let you have it back, Ron."

Ron had expected that, and was too keen for explanations to protest.

 "Because...," Weasley hesitated, "because these mapmakers would have wanted to lure you out of school. They'd think it extremely entertaining."

"Do you know them?" said Ron, impressed.

"We've met," he said shortly. He was looking at Ron more seriously than ever before.

"Don't expect me to cover up for you again, Ron. I cannot make you take Ron Weasley seriously. But I would have thought that what you have heard when the dementors draw near you would have had more of an effect on you. Your parents gave their lives to keep you alive, Ron. A poor way to repay them ­­ gambling their sacrifice for a bag of magic tricks."

He walked away, leaving Ron feeling worse by far than he had at any point in Weasley's office. Slowly, he and Ron mounted the marble staircase. As Ron passed the one­eyed witch, he remembered the Invisibility Cloak ­­ it was still down there, but he didn't dare go and get it.

He broke off; they reached the corridor where the security trolls were pacing, and Ron was walking toward them. One look at her face convinced Ron that she had heard what had happened. His heart plummeted ­­ had she told Professor Weasley?

"No," said Ron. She was holding a letter in her hands and her lip was trembling. "I just thought you ought to know... Weasley lost his case. Ron is going to be executed."

He sent me this," Ron said, holding out the letter.

 He seemed numb with shock at the verdict.

The Easter holidays were not exactly relaxing. The third years had never had so much homework. Ron Weasley seemed close to a nervous collapse, and he wasn't the only one.

"Call this a holiday!" Ron Weasley roared at the common room one afternoon. "The exams are ages away, what're they playing at?"

Ron had taken over responsibility for Ron's appeal. When he wasn't doing his own work, he was poring over enormously thick volumes with names like The Handbook of Hippogriff Psychology and Fowl or Foul? A Study of Hippogriff Brutality. He was so absorbed, he even forgot to be horrible to Ron.

 Ron, meanwhile, had to fit in his homework around Quidditch practice every day, not to mention endless discussions of tactics with Weasley. The Weasley­Weasley match would take place on the first Saturday after the Easter holidays. Weasley was leading the tournament by exactly two hundred points. This meant (as Weasley constantly reminded his team) that they needed to win the match by more than that amount to win the Cup. It also meant that the burden of winning fell largely on Ron, because capturing the Snitch was worth one hundred and fifty points.

The whole of Weasley House was obsessed with the coming match.

Weasley hadn't won the Quidditch Cup since the legendary Ron Weasley (Ron's second oldest brother) had been seeker. But Ron doubted whether any of them, even Weasley, wanted to win as much as he did. The enmity between Ron and Weasley was at its highest point ever. Never, in anyone's memory, had a match approached in such a highly charged atmosphere. By the time the holidays were over, tension between the two teams and their Houses was at the breaking point.  CHAPTER SIXTEEN PROFESSOR Weasley'S PREDICTION

Ron's euphoria at finally winning the Quidditch Cup lasted at least a week. Even the weather seemed to be celebrating; as June approached, the days became cloudless and sultry, and all anybody felt like doing was strolling onto the grounds and flopping down on the grass with several pints of iced pumpkin juice, perhaps playing a casual game of Gobstones or watching the giant squid propel itself dreamily across the surface of the lake.

But they couldn't. Exams were nearly upon them, and instead of lazing around outside, the students were forced to remain inside the castle,

trying to bully their brains into concentrating while enticing wafts of summer air drifted in through the windows. Even Ron and Ron Weasley had been spotted working; they were about to take their O.W.L.s (Ordinary Wizarding Levels). Ron was getting ready to take his N.E.W.T.s (Nastily Exhausting Wizarding Tests), the highest qualification Hogwarts offered. As Ron hoped to enter the Ministry of Magic, he needed top grades. He was becoming increasingly edgy, and gave very severe punishments to anybody who disturbed the quiet of the common room in the evenings. In fact, the only person who seemed more anxious than Ron was Ron.

Ron and Ron had given up asking her how she was managing to attend several classes at once, but they couldn't restrain themselves when they saw the exam schedule she had drawn up for herself. The first column read:

They had Potions that afternoon, which was an unqualified disaster. Try as Ron might, he couldn't get his Confusing Concoction to thicken, and Weasley, standing watch with an air of vindictive pleasure, scribbled something that looked suspiciously like a zero onto his notes before moving away.

Then came Astronomy at midnight, up on the tallest tower; History of Magic on Wednesday morning, in which Ron scribbled everything Ron Weasley had ever told him about medieval witch­hunts, while wishing he could have had one of Weasley's choco­nut sundaes with him in the stifling classroom. Wednesday afternoon meant Herbology, in the greenhouses under a baking­hot sun; then back to the common room once more, with sunburnt necks, thinking longingly of this time next day,

when it would all be over.

 CHAPTER SEVENTEEN CAT, RAT, AND DOG

Ron reached for his wand, but too late ­­ the dog had made an enormous leap and the front paws hit him on the chest; he keeled over backward in a whirl of hair; he felt its hot breath, saw inch­ long teeth ­ But the force of its leap had carried it too far; it rolled off him.

Dazed, feeling as though his ribs were broken, Ron tried to stand up; he could hear it growling as it skidded around for a new attack.

Ron was on his feet. As the dog sprang back toward them he pushed Ron aside; the dog's jaws fastened instead around Ron's outstretched arm.

Ron lunged forward, he seized a handful of the brute's hair, but it was dragging Ron away as easily as though he were a rag doll ­­ Then, out of nowhere, something hit Ron so hard across the face he was knocked off his feet again. He heard Ron shriek with pain and fall too.

Ron groped for his wand, blinking blood out of his eyes "Lumos!"he whispered.

 The wandlight showed him the trunk of a thick tree; they had chased Ron into the shadow of the Whomping Willow and its branches were creaking as though in a high wind, whipping backward and forward to stop them going nearer.

And there, at the base of the trunk, was the dog, dragging Ron backward into a large gap in the roots ­­ Ron was fighting furiously, but his head and torso were slipping out of sight ­­ "Ron!" Ron shouted, trying to follow, but a heavy branch whipped lethally through the air and he was forced backward again.

All they could see now was one of Ron's legs, which he had hooked around a root in an effort to stop the dog from pulling him farther underground ­­ but a horrible crack cut the air like a gunshot; Ron's leg had broken, and a moment later, his foot vanished from sight.

"Ron ­­ we've got to go for help ­­" Ron gasped; she was bleeding too; the Willow had cut her across the shoulder.

"No! That thing's big enough to eat him; we haven't got time ­­"

Ron darted forward. He slithered between the battering branches like a snake and placed his front paws upon a knot on the trunk.

Abruptly, as though the tree had been turned to marble, it stopped moving. Not a leaf twitched or shook.

 "Ron!" Ron whispered uncertainly. She now grasped Ron's arm painfully hard. "How did he know ­­?"

They covered the distance to the trunk in seconds, but before they had reached the gap in the roots, Ron had slid into it with a flick of his bottlebrush tail. Ron went next; he crawled forward, headfirst,

and slid down an earthy slope to the bottom of a very low tunnel.

Ron was a little way along, his eyes flashing in the light from Ron's wand. Seconds later, Ron slithered down beside him.

but it looked like it was heading for Hogsmeade..."

They moved as fast as they could, bent almost double; ahead of them,

Ron's tail bobbed in and out of view. On and on went the passage; it felt at least as long as the one to Honeydukes.... All Ron could think of was Ron and what the enormous dog might be doing to him.... He was drawing breath in sharp, painful gasps, running at a crouch....

And then the tunnel began to rise; moments later it twisted, and Ron had gone. instead, Ron could see a patch of dim light through a small opening.

He and Ron paused, gasping for breath, edging forward. Both raised their wands to see what lay beyond.

was broken as though somebody had smashed it. The windows were all boarded up.

Ron glanced at Ron, who looked very frightened but nodded.

At that moment, there was a creak overhead. Something had Moved upstairs. Both of them looked up at the ceiling. Ron's grip on Ron's arm was so tight he was losing feeling in­his fingers. He raised his eyebrows at her; she nodded again and let go.

Quietly as they could, they crept out into the hall and UP the crumbling staircase. Everything was covered in a thick layer of dust except the floor, where a wide shiny stripe had been made by something being dragged upstairs.

They reached the dark landing.

"Nox," they whispered together, and the lights at the end of their wands went out. Only one door was open. As they crept toward it, they heard movement from behind it; a low moan, and then a deep, loud purring. They exchanged a last look, a last nod.

Wand held tightly before him, Ron kicked the door wide open.

"There'll be only one murder here tonight," said Brack, and his grin widened.

I sometimes felt guilty about betraying Weasley's trust, of course...

he had admitted me to Hogwarts when no other headmaster would have done so, and he had no idea I was breaking the rules he had set down for my own and others' safety. He never knew I had led three fellow students into becoming Animagi illegally. But I always managed to forget my guilty feelings every time we sat down to plan our next month's adventure. And I haven't changed..."

Weasley's face had hardened, and there was self­disgust in his voice. "All this year, I have been battling with myself, wondering whether I should tell Weasley that Ron was an Animagus. But I didn't do it. Why?

Because I was too cowardly. It would have meant admitting that I'd betrayed his trust while I was at school, admitting that I'd led others along with me... and Weasley's trust has meant everything to me. He let me into Hogwarts as a boy, and he gave me a job when I have been shunned all my adult life, unable to find paid work because of what I am. And so I convinced myself that Ron was getting into the school using dark arts he learned from Weasley, that being an Animagus had nothing to do with it... so, in a way, Weasley's been right about me all along."

"Weasley?" said Weasley harshly, taking his eyes off Ron; for the first time in minutes and looking up at Weasley. "What's Weasley got to do with it?"

"He's here, Ron," said Weasley heavily. "He's teaching here as well."

He looked up at Ron, Ron, and Ron.

"Professor Weasley was at school with us. He fought very hard against my appointment to the Defense Against the Dark Arts job. He has been telling Weasley A year that I am not to be trusted. He has his reasons... you see, Ron here played a trick on him which nearly killed him, a trick which involved me ­­"

Weasley made a derisive noise.

 "It served him right," he sneered. "Sneaking around, trying to find out what we were up to... hoping he could get us expelled...."

"Ron was very interested in where I went every month." Weasley told Ron, Ron, and Ron. "We were in the same year, you know, and we ­­ er ­­ didn't like each other very much. He especially disliked Ron.

Jealous, I think, of Ron's talent on the Quidditch field... anyway Weasley had seen me crossing the grounds with Ron Weasley one evening as she led me toward the Whomping Willow to transform. Ron thought it would be ­­ er ­­ amusing, to tell Weasley all he had to do was prod the knot on the tree trunk with a long stick, and he'd be able to get in after me. Well, of course, Weasley tried it ­­ if he'd got as far as this house, he'd have met a fully grown werewolf ­­ but your father, who'd heard what Ron had done, went after Weasley and pulled him back, at great risk to his life... Weasley glimpsed me, though, at the end of the tunnel. He was forbidden by Weasley to tell anybody, but from that time on he knew what I was...."

"So that's why Weasley doesn't like you," said Ron slowly, "because he thought you were in on the joke?"

"That's right," sneered a cold voice from the wall behind Weasley.

Ron Weasley was pulling off the Invisibility Cloak, his wand pointing,

directly at Weasley.

 CHAPTER NINETEEN THE SERVANT OF LORD Weasley

Ron screamed. Weasley leapt to his feet. Ron felt as though he'd received a huge electric shock.

He was quite convinced you were harmless, you know, Weasley... a tame werewolf ­­"

Weasley started toward Weasley, but Weasley pointed his wand straight between Weasley's eyes.

Weasley stopped dead. It would have been impossible to say which face showed more hatred.

What little color there was in Weasleys face left it.

Perhaps the dementors will have a kiss for him too ­­"

Ron made up his mind in a split second. Before Weasley could take even one step toward him, he had raised his wand.

He was pointing at Weasley, who shook his head slowly; the sunken eyes were suddenly over bright.

His voice broke. He turned away.

without turning a hair. You heard him. His own stinking skin meant more to him than your whole family."

"Ron!" gasped Weasley, and he flung his arms around Ron's knees.

"You ­­ thank you ­­ it's more than I deserve ­­ thank you ­­"

"Get off me," Ron spat, throwing Weasley's hands off him in disgust.

"I'm not doing this for you. I'm doing it because ­­ I don't reckon my dad would've wanted them to become killers ­­ just for you."

No one moved or made a sound except Weasley, whose breath was coming in wheezes as he clutched his chest. Weasley and Weasley were looking at each other. Then, with one movement, they lowered their wands.

"You're the only person who has the right to decide, Ron," said Weasley.

"But think... think what he did...."

"He can go to Azkaban," Ron repeated. "If anyone deserves that place,

he does...."

Weasley was still wheezing behind him.

 "Very well," said Weasley. "Rond aside, Ron."

Ron hesitated.

"I'm going to tie him up," said Weasley. "That's all, I swear."

Ron stepped out of the way. Thin cords shot from Weasley's wand this time, and next moment, Weasley was wriggling on the floor, bound and gagged.

"But if you transform, Ron," growled Weasley, his own wand pointing at Weasley too, "we will kill you. You agree, Ron?"

Ron looked down at the pitiful figure on the floor and nodded so that Weasley could see him.

"Right," said Weasley, suddenly businesslike. "Ron, I can't mend bones nearly as well as Ron Weasley, so I think it's best if we just strap your leg up until we can get you to the hospital wing."

He hurried over to Ron, bent down, tapped Ron's leg with his wand, and muttered, "Ferula." Bandages spun up Ron's leg, strapping it tightly to a splint. Weasley helped him to his feet; Ron put his weight gingerly on the leg and didn't wince.

"That's better," he said. "Thanks."

"What about Professor Weasley?" said Ron in a small voice, looking down at Weasley's prone figure.

"There's nothing seriously wrong with him," said Weasley, bending over Weasley and checking his pulse. "You were just a little ­­ overenthusiastic. Still out cold. Er ­­ perhaps it will be best if we don't revive him until we're safety back in the castle. We can take him like this...."

He muttered, "Mobilicorpus." As though invisible strings were tied to Weasley's wrists, neck, and knees, he was pulled into a standing position,

head still lolling unpleasantly, like a grotesque puppet. He hung a few

inches above the ground, his limp feet dangling. Weasley picked up the Invisibility Cloak and tucked it safely into his pocket.

"And two of us should be chained to this," said Weasley, nudging Weasley with his toe. "Just to make sure."

"I'll do it," said Weasley.

"And me," said Ron savagely, limping forward.

Weasley conjured heavy manacles from thin air; soon Weasley was upright again, left arm chained to Weasley's right, right arm to Ron's left. Ron's face was set. He seemed to have taken Ron's true identity as a personal insult. Ron leapt lightly off the bed and led the way out of the room, his bottlebrush tail held jauntily high.

 CHAPTER TWENTY THE DEMENTOR'S KISS

Ron had never been part of a stranger group. Ron led the way down the stairs; Weasley, Weasley, and Ron went next, looking like entrants in a six­legged race. Next came Professor Weasley, drifting creepily along, his toes hitting each stair as they descended, held up by his own wand, which was being pointed at him by Ron. Ron and Ron brought up the rear.

Getting back into the tunnel was difficult. Weasley, Weasley, and Ron had to turn sideways to manage it; Weasley still had Weasley covered with his wand. Ron could see them edging awkwardly along the tunnel in single file. Ron was still in the lead. Ron went right after Weasley, who was still making Weasley drift along ahead of them; he kept bumping his lolling head on the low ceiling. Ron had the impression Weasley was making no effort to prevent this.

"You know what this means?" Weasley said abruptly to Ron as they made their slow progress along the tunnel. "Turning Weasley in?"

"You' re free," said Ron.

 "Yes...," said Weasley. "But I'm also ­­ I don't know if anyone ever told you ­­ I'm your godfather."

"Yeah, I knew that," said Ron.

"Well... your parents appointed me your guardian," said Weasley stiffly.

"If anything happened to them..."

Ron waited. Did Weasley mean what he thought he meant?

"I'll understand, of course, if you want to stay with your aunt and uncle," said Weasley. "But... well... think about it. Once my name's cleared... if you wanted a... a different home..."

Some sort of explosion took place in the pit of Ron's stomach.

"What ­­ live with you?" he said, accidentally cracking his head on a bit of rock protruding from the ceiling. "Leave the Weasleys?"

"Of course, I thought you wouldn't want to," said Weasley quickly. "I understand, I just thought I'd ­­"

"Are you insane?" said Ron, his voice easily as croaky as Weasley's.

"Of course I want to leave the Weasleys! Have you got a house? When can I move in?"

Weasley turned right around to look at him; Weasley's head was scraping the ceiling but Weasley didn't seem to care.

"You want to?" he said. "You mean it?"

"Yeah, I mean it!" said Ron.

Weasley's gaunt face broke into the first true smile Ron had seen upon it. The difference it made was startling, as though a person ten years younger were shining through the starved mask; for a moment, he was recognizable as the man who had laughed at Ron's parents' wedding.

They did not speak again until they had reached the end of the tunnel.

 Ron darted up first; he had evidently pressed his paw to the knot on the trunk, because Weasley, Weasley, and Ron clambered upward without any sound of savaging branches.

Weasley saw Weasley up through the hole, then stood back for Ron and Ron to pass. At last, all of them were out.

The grounds were very dark now; the only light came from the distant windows of the castle. Without a word, they set off. Weasley was still wheezing and occasionally whimpering. Ron's mind was buzzing. He was going to leave the Weasleys. He was going to live with Ron Weasley, his parents' best friend.... He felt dazed.... What would happen when he told the Weasleys he was going to live with the convict they'd seen on television... !

"One wrong move, Ron," said Weasley threateningly ahead. His wand was still pointed sideways at Weasley's chest.

Silently they tramped through the grounds, the castle lights growing slowly larger. Weasley was still drifting weirdly ahead of Weasley, his chin bumping on his chest. And then ­ A cloud shifted. There were suddenly dim shadows on the ground. Their party was bathed in moonlight.

Weasley collided with Weasley, Weasley, and Ron, who had stopped abruptly.

Weasley froze. He flung out one arm to make Ron and Ron stop.

Ron could see Weasley's silhouette. He had gone rigid. Then his limbs began to shake.

"Oh, my ­­" Ron gasped. "He didn't take his potion tonight! He's not safe!"

"Run," Weasley whispered. "Run. Now."

But Ron couldn't run. Ron was chained to Weasley and Weasley. He leapt forward but Weasley caught him around the chest and threw him back.

"Leave it to me ­­ RUN!"

 There was a terrible snarling noise. Weasley's head was lengthening. So was his body. His shoulders were hunching. Hair was sprouting visibly on his face and hands, which were curling into clawed paws. Ron's hair was on end again; he was backing away ­­ As the werewolf reared, snapping its long jaws, Ron disappeared from Ron's side. He had transformed. The enormous, bearlike dog bounded forward. As the werewolf wrenched itself free of the manacle binding it,

the dog seized it about the neck and pulled it backward, away from Ron and Weasley. They were locked, jaw to jaw, claws ripping at each other.

Ron stood, transfixed by the sight, too intent upon the battle to notice anything else. It was Ron's scream that alerted him ­­ Weasley had dived for Weasley's dropped wand. Ron, unsteady on his bandaged leg, fell. There was a bang, a burst of light ­­ and Ron lay motionless on the ground. Another bang ­­ Ron flew into the air and back to the earth in a heap.

"Expelliarmus." Ron yelled, pointing his own wand at Weasley; Weasley's wand flew high into the air and out of sight. "Stay where you are!" Ron shouted, running forward.

Too late. Weasley had transformed. Ron saw his bald tail whip through the manacle on Ron's outstretched arm and heard a scurrying through the grass.

There was a howl and a rumbling growl; Ron turned to see the werewolf taking flight; it was galloping into the forest ­­ "Ron, he's gone, Weasley transformed!" Ron yelled.

Weasley was bleeding; there were gashes across his muzzle and back, but at Ron's words he scrambled up again, and in an instant, the sound of his paws faded to silence as he pounded away across the grounds.

Ron and Ron dashed over to Ron.

"What did he do to him?" Ron whispered. Ron's eyes were only

half­closed, his mouth hung open; he was definitely alive, they could hear him breathing, but he didn't seem to recognize them.

"I don't know...."

Ron looked desperately around. Weasley and Weasley both gone... they had no one but Weasley for company, still hanging, unconscious, in midair.

"We'd better get them up to the castle and tell someone," said Ron,

pushing his hair out of his eyes, trying to think straight. "Come ­­"

But then, from beyond the range of their vision, they heard a yelping, a whining: a dog in pain....

"Ron," Ron muttered, staring into the darkness.

He had a moment's indecision, but there was nothing they could do for Ron at the moment, and by the sound of it, Weasley was in trouble ­­ Ron set off at a run, Ron right behind him. The yelping seemed to be coming from the ground near the edge of the lake. They pelted toward it, and Ron, running flat out, felt the cold without realizing what it must mean ­ The yelping stopped abruptly. As they reached the lakeshore, they saw why ­­ Ron had turned back into a man. He was crouched on all fours,

his hands over his head.

'Nooo," he moaned. 'Nooo... please...."

And then Ron saw them. Dementors, at least a hundred of them, gliding in a black mass around the lake toward them. He spun around, the familiar, icy cold penetrating his insides, fog starting to obscure his vision; more were appearing out of the darkness on every side; they were encircling them....

"Herrnione, think of something happy!" Ron yelled, raising his wand,

blinking furiously to try and clear his vision, shaking his head to rid it of the faint screaming that had started inside it ­­

I'm going to live with my godfather. I'm leaving the Weasleys.

He forced himself to think of Weasley, and only Weasley, and began to chant:

"Expecto patronum! Expecto patronum!"

Weasley gave a shudder, rolled over, and lay motionless on the ground,

pale as death.

He'll be all right. I'm going to go and live with him.

"Expecto patronum! Ron, help me! Expecto patronum!"

"Expecto ­­" Ron whispered, "expecto ­­ expecto ­­"

But she couldn't do it. The dementors were closing in, barely ten feet from them. They formed a solid wall around Ron and Ron, and were getting closer....

"EXPECTO PATRONUM!" Ron yelled, trying to blot the screaming from his ears. "EXPECTO PATRONUM!"

A thin wisp of silver escaped his wand and hovered like mist before him.

At the same moment, Ron felt Ron collapse next to him. He was alone... completely alone....

"Expecto ­­ expecto patronum ­­"

Ron felt his knees hit the cold grass. Fog was clouding his eyes. With a huge effort, he fought to remember ­­ Ron was innocent ­­ innocent ­­ We'll be okay ­­ I' mgoing to live with him ­­ "Ex ecto patronum!" he gasped.

By the feeble light of his formless Patronus, He saw a dementor halt,

very close to him. It couldn't walk through the cloud of silver mist Ron had conjured. A dead, slimy hand slid out from under the cloak. It made a gesture as though to sweep the Patronus aside.

"No ­­ no ­­" Ron gasped. "He's innocent... expecto expecto patronum ­­"

 He could feet them watching him, hear their rattling breath like an evil wind around him. The nearest dementor seemed to be considering him. Then it raised both its rotting hands ­­ and lowered its hood.

Where there should have been eyes, there was only thin, gray scabbed skin, stretched blankly over empty sockets. But there was a mouth... a gaping, shapeless hole, sucking the air with the sound of a death rattle.

A paralyzing terror filled Ron so that he couldn't move or speak. His Patronus flickered and died.

White fog was blinding him. He had to fight... expecto patronum ... he couldn't see... and in the distance, he heard the familiar screaming...

expecto patronum... he groped in the mist for Ron, and found his arm... they weren't going to take him....

But a pair of strong, clammy hands suddenly attached themselves around Ron's neck. They were forcing his face upward.... He could feel its breath.... It was going to get rid of him first.... He could feel its putrid breath.... His mother was screaming in his ears.... She was going to be the last thing he ever heard ­­ And then, through the fog that was drowning him, he thought he saw a silvery light growing brighter and brighter... He felt himself fall forward onto the grass.... Facedown, too weak to move, sick and shaking,

Ron opened his eyes. The dementor must have released him. The blinding light was illuminating the grass around him.... The screaming had stopped, the cold was ebbing away...

Something was driving the dementors back.... It was circling around him and Weasley and Ron.... They were leaving....

The air was warm again....

With every ounce of strength he could muster, Ron raised his head a few inches and saw an animal amid the light, galloping away across the lake.... Eyes blurred with sweat, Ron tried to make out what it was.... It was as bright as a unicorn.... Fighting to stay conscious,

 Ron watched it canter to a halt as it reached the opposite shore. For a moment, Ron saw, by its brightness, somebody welcoming it back...

raising his hand to pat it... someone who looked strangely familiar ...

but it couldn't be...

Ron didn't understand. He couldn't think anymore. He felt the last of his strength leave him, and his head hit the ground as he fainted.

 CHAPTER TWENTY­ONE Ron'S SECRET

Shocking business... shocking... miracle none of them died... never heard the like... by thunder, it was lucky you were there, Weasley...."

"Thank you, Minister."

"Order of Merlin, Second Class, I'd say. First Class, if I can wangle it!"

"Thank you very much indeed, Minister."

"As a matter of fact, it was Weasley, Weasley, and Weasley, Minister...."

They weren't responsible for their actions. On the other hand, their interference might have permitted Weasley to escape.... They obviously thought they were going to catch Weasley single­handed. They've got away with a great deal before now... I'm afraid it's given them a rather high opinion of themselves... and of course Weasley has always been allowed an extraordinary amount of license by the headmaster ­­"

Personally, I try and treat him like any other student. And any other student would be suspended ­­ at the very least ­­ for leading his friends into such danger. Ron lay listening with his eyes tight shut. He felt very groggy. The words he was hearing seemed to be traveling very slowly from his ears to his brain, so that it was difficult to understand.... His limbs felt like lead; his eyelids too heavy to lift.... He wanted to lie here, on this comfortable bed, forever....

"All unconscious by the time I reached them. I bound and gagged Weasley,

naturally, conjured stretchers, and brought them all straight back to the castle."

There was a pause. Ron's brain seemed to be moving a little faster,

and as it did, a gnawing sensation grew in the pit of his stomach....

He opened his eyes.

Everything was slightly blurred. Somebody had removed his glasses. He was lying in the dark hospital wing. At the very end of the ward, he could make out Ron Weasley with her back to him, bending over a bed.

Ron squinted. Ron's red hair was visible beneath Ron Weasley's arm.

 Ron moved his head over on the pillow. In the bed to his right lay Ron. Moonlight was falling across her bed. Her eyes were open too.

She looked petrified, and when she saw that Ron was awake, pressed a finger to her lips, then pointed to the hospital wing door. It was ajar,

and the voices of Ron Weasley and Weasley were coming through it from the corridor outside.

Ron Weasley now came walking briskly up the dark ward to Ron's bed.

He turned to took at her. She was carrying the largest block of chocolate he had ever seen in his life. It looked like a small boulder.

"Ah, you're awake!" she said briskly. She placed the chocolate on Ron's bedside table and began breaking it apart with a small hammer.

"How's Ron?" said Ron and Ron together.

"He'll live, said Ron Weasley grimly. "As for you two you'll be staying here until I'm satisfied you're ­­ Weasley, what do you think you're doing?"

Ron was sitting up, putting his glasses back on, and picking up his wand.

"I need to see the headmaster," he said.

"Weasley," said Ron Weasley soothingly, "it's all right. They've got Weasley. He's locked away upstairs. The dementors will be performing the kiss any moment now ­­"

Ron jumped up out of bed; Ron had done the same. But his shout had been heard in the corridor outside; next second, Ron Weasley and Weasley had entered the ward.

Weasley faked his own death! We saw him tonight! You can't let the dementors do that thing to Ron, he's ­­"

But Weasley was shaking his head with a small smile on his face.

"YOU HAVEN'T!" Ron yelled. "YOUVE GOT THE WRONG MAN!"

But Ron Weasley suddenly stuffed a large chunk of chocolate into Ron's mouth; he choked, and she seized the opportunity to force him back onto the bed.

"Now, please, Minister, these children need care. Please leave The door opened again. It was Weasley. Ron swallowed his mouthful of chocolate with great difficulty and got up again.

"My apologies, Ron, but I need a word with Mr. Weasley and Miss Weasley," said Weasley calmly. "I have just been talking to Ron Weasley ­­"

 "I suppose he's told you the same fairy tale he's planted in Weasley's mind?" spat Weasley. "Something about a rat, and Weasley being alive ­­"

"That, indeed, is Weasley's story," said Weasley, surveying Weasley closely through his half­moon spectacles.

"And does my evidence count for nothing?" snarled Weasley. "Ron Weasley was not in the Shrieking Shack, nor did I see any sign of him on the grounds."

"That was because you were knocked out, Professor!" said Ron earnestly. "You didn't arrive in time to hear "Miss Weasley, HOLD YOUR TONGUE!"

Ron Weasley pursed her lips and strode away into her office at the end of the ward, slamming the door behind her. Weasley consulted the large gold pocket watch dangling from his waistcoat.

"The dementors should have arrived by now," he said. "I'll go and meet them. Weasley, I'll see you upstairs."

He crossed to the door and held it open for Weasley, but Weasley hadn't moved.

 "I wish to speak to Ron and Ron alone," Weasley repeated.

Weasley took a step toward Weasley.

"My memory is as good as it ever was, Ron," said Weasley quietly.

Weasley turned on his heel and marched through the door Weasley was still holding. It closed behind them, and Weasley turned to Ron and Ron. They both burst into speech at the same time.

A street full of eyewitnesses swore they saw Ron murder Weasley. I myself gave evidence to the Ministry that Ron had been the Weasleys' Secret­Keeper."

Ron stared up into the grave face and felt as though the ground beneath him were falling sharply away. He had grown used to the idea that Weasley could solve anything. He had expected Weasley to pull some amazing solution out of the air. But no ... their last hope was gone.

"What we need," said Weasley slowly, and his light blue eyes moved from Ron to Ron, "is more time."

Ron didn't have a clue what was going on. Weasley had turned on his heel and looked back as he reached the door.

 "I am going to lock you in. It is ­­" he consulted his watch, "five minutes to midnight. Miss Weasley, three turns should do it. Good luck."

But Ron was fumbling with the neck of her robes, pulling from beneath them a very long, very fine gold chain.

Ron moved toward her, completely bewildered. She was holding the chain out. He saw a tiny, sparkling hourglass hanging from it.

"Here ­­"

She had thrown the chain around his neck too.

Ron turned the hourglass over three times.

The dark ward dissolved. Ron had the sensation that he was flying very fast, backward. He looked wildly around at Ron, the chain of the hourglass cutting into his neck.

"In here!" Ron seized Ron's arm and dragged him across the hall

to the door of a broom closet; she opened it, pushed him inside among the buckets and mops, then slammed the door behind them.

Ron found his own leg and gave it a very hard pinch. It hurt a lot,

which seemed to rule out the possibility that he was having a very bizarre dream.

Ron had her ear pressed against the cupboard door.

She broke off, still listening intently.

but Ron wanted a few questions answered.

Magic so I could have one. She had to tell them that I was a model student, and that I'd never, ever use it for anything except my studies.... I've been turning it back so I could do hours over again,

that's how I've been doing several lessons at once, see? But...

Come on, let's go."

Ron pushed open the closet door. The entrance hall was deserted. As quietly and quickly as they could, they darted out of the closet and

down the stone steps. The shadows were already lengthening, the tops of the trees in the Forbidden Forest gilded once more with gold.

all right? We'll have to hide behind a tree or something and keep a lookout ­­"

BAM.

The door of the hospital wing burst open.

Weasley, Weasley, and Weasley came striding into the ward. Weasley alone looked calm. Indeed, he looked as though he was quite enjoying himself. Weasley appeared angry. But Weasley was beside himself.

"OUT WITH IT, Weasley!" he bellowed. "WHAT DID YOU DO?"

"Professor Weasley!" shrieked Ron Weasley. "Control yourself!"

"See here, Weasley, be reasonable," said Weasley. "This door's been locked,

we just saw ­­"

"THEY HELPED HIM ESCAPE, I KNOW IT!" Weasley howled, pointing at Ron and Ron. His face was twisted; spit was flying from his mouth.

"Calm down, man!" Weasley barked. "You're talking nonsense!"

"YOU DON'T KNOW Weasley!" shrieked Weasley. "HE DID IT, I KNOW HE DID IT ­­"

"That will do, Ron," said Weasley quietly. "Think about what you are saying. This door has been locked since I left the ward ten minutes ago. Ron Weasley, have these students left their beds?"

 "Of course not!" said Ron Weasley, bristling. "I would have heard them!"

"Well, there you have it, Ron," said Weasley calmly. "Unless you are suggesting that Ron and Ron are able to be in two places at once, I'm afraid I don't see any point in troubling them further."

Weasley stood there, seething, staring from Weasley, who looked thoroughly shocked at his behavior, to Weasley, whose eyes were twinkling behind his glasses. Weasley whirled about, robes swishing behind him, and stormed out of the ward.

"Fellow seems quite unbalanced," said Weasley, staring after him. "I'd watch out for him if I were you, Weasley."

"Oh, he's not unbalanced," said Weasley quietly. "He's just suffered a severe disappointment."

"He's not the only one!" puffed Weasley. "The Daily Prophet's going to have a field day! We had Weasley cornered and he slipped through our fingers yet again! All it needs now is for the story of that hippogriff's escape to get out, and I'll be a laughingstock! Well... I'd better go and notify the Ministry.....

"And the dementors?" said Weasley. "They'll be removed from the school, I trust?"

"Oh yes, they'll have to go," said Weasley, running his fingers distractedly through his hair. "Never dreamed they'd attempt to administer the Kiss on an innocent boy... Completely out of control...

no, I'll have them packed off back to Azkaban tonight.... Perhaps we should think about dragons at the school entrance...."

"Weasley would like that," said Weasley, smiling at Ron and Ron. As he and Weasley left the dormitory, Ron Weasley hurried to the door and locked it again. Muttering angrily to herself, she headed back to her office.

There was a low moan from the other end of the ward. Ron had woken up.

 They could see him sitting up, rubbing his head, looking around.

"What ­­ what happened?" he groaned. "Ron? Why are we in here? Where's Ron? Where's Weasley? What's going on?"

Ron and Ron looked at each other.

"You explain," said Ron, helping himself to some more chocolate.

When Ron, Ron, and Ron left the hospital wing at noon the next day, it was to find an almost deserted castle. The sweltering, heat and the end of the exams meant that everyone was taking full advantage of another Hogsmeade visit. Neither Ron nor Ron felt like going,

however, so they and Ron wandered onto the grounds, still talking about the extraordinary events of the previous night and wondering where Ron and Ron were now. Sitting near the lake, watching the giant squid waving its tentacles lazily above the water, Ron lost the thread of the conversation as he looked across to the opposite bank. The stag had galloped toward him from there just last night....

A shadow fell across them and they looked 'tip to see a very bleary­eyed Weasley, mopping his sweaty face with one of his tablecloth­sized handkerchiefs and beaming down at them.

"Know I shouldn' feel happy, after wha' happened las' night," he said.

"I mean, Weasley escapin' again, an, everythin' ­­ but guess what?"

"What?" they said, pretending to look curious.

"Beaky! He escaped! He's free! Bin celebratin' all night!"

"That's wonderful!" said Ron, giving Ron a reproving look because he looked as though he was close to laughing.

"Yeah... can't've tied him up properly," said Weasley, gazing happily out over the grounds. "I was worried this mornin', mind... thought he mighta met Professor Weasley on the grounds, but Weasley says he never ate anythin' las' night...."

"What?" said Ron quickly.

 "Blimey, haven' yeh heard?" said Weasley, his smile fading a little. He lowered his voice, even though there was nobody in sight. "Er ­­ Weasley told all the Weasleys this mornin'.... Thought everyone'd know by now... Professor Weasley's a werewolf, see. An' he was loose on the grounds las' night.... He's packin' now, o' course.

"He's packing?" said Ron, alarmed. "Why?"

"Leavin', isn' he?" said Weasley, looking surprised that Ron had to ask. "Resigned firs' thing this mornin'. Says he can't risk it happenin again.

Ron scrambled to his feet.

"I'm going to see him," he said to Ron and Ron.

"But if he's resigned ­­"

"­­ doesn't sound like there's anything we can do ­­"

"I don't care. I still want to see him. I'll meet you back here."

Weasley's office door was open. He had already packed most of his things.

The grindylow's empty tank stood next to his battered old suitcase,

which was open and nearly full. Weasley was bending over something on his desk and looked up only when Ron knocked on the door.

"I saw you coming," said Weasley, smiling. He pointed to the parchment he had been poring over. It was the Marauder's Map.

"I just saw Weasley," said Ron. "And he said you'd resigned. It's not true, is it?"

"I'm afraid it is," said Weasley. He started opening his desk drawers and taking out the contents.

"Why?" said Ron. "The Ministry of Magic don't think you were helping Ron, do they?"

 Weasley crossed to the door and closed it behind Ron.

"No. Professor Weasley managed to convince Weasley that I was trying to save your lives." He sighed. "That was the final straw for Ron. I think the loss of the Order of Merlin hit him hard. So he ­­ er ­­ accidentally let slip that I am a werewolf this morning at breakfast."

"You're not leaving just because of that!" said Ron.

Weasley smiled wryly.

"This time tomorrow, the owls will start arriving from parents.... They will not want a werewolf teaching their children, Ron. And after last night, I see their point. I could have bitten any of you.... That must never happen again."

"You're the best Defense Against the Dark Arts­ teacher we've ever had!"

said Ron. "Don't go!"

Weasley shook his head and didn't speak. He carried on emptying his drawers. Then, while Ron was trying to think of a good argument to make him stay, Weasley said, "From what the headmaster told me this morning, you saved a lot of lives last night, Ron. if I'm proud of anything I've done this year, it's how much you've learned.... Tell me about your Patronus."

"How d'you know about that?" said Ron, distracted.

"What else could have driven the dementors back?"

Ron told Weasley what had happened. When he'd finished, Weasley was smiling again.

"Yes, your father was always a stag when he transformed," he said. "You guessed right... that's why we called him Prongs."

Weasley threw his last few books into his case, closed the desk drawers,

and turned to look at Ron.

"Here ­­ I brought this from the Shrieking Shack last night," he said,

 handing Ron back the Invisibility Cloak. "And..." He hesitated, then held out the Marauder's Map too. "I am no longer your teacher, so I don't feel guilty about giving you back this as well. It's no use to me,

and I daresay you, Ron, and Ron will find uses for it."

Ron took the map and grinned.

"You told me Moony, Wormtail, Padfoot, and Prongs would've wanted to lure me out of school... you said they'd have thought it was funny."

"And so we would have," said Weasley, now reaching down to close his case.

"I have no hesitation in saying that Ron would have been highly disappointed if his son had never found any of the secret passages out of the castle."

There was a knock on the door. Ron hastily stuffed the Marauder's Map and the Invisibility Cloak into his pocket.

It was Professor Weasley. He didn't look surprised to see Ron there.

"Your carriage is at the gates, Ron," he said.

"Thank You, Headmaster."

Weasley picked up his old suitcase and the empty grindylow tank.

"Well ­­ good­bye, Ron," he said, smiling. "It has been a real pleasure teaching you. I feel sure we'll meet again sometime.

Headmaster, there is no need to see me to the gates, I can manage...."

Ron had the impression that Weasley wanted to leave as quickly as possible.

"Good­bye, then, Ron," said Weasley soberly. Weasley shifted the grindylow tank slightly so that he and Weasley could shake hands.

Then, with a final nod to Ron and a swift smile, Weasley left the office.

Ron sat down in his vacated chair, staring glumly at the floor. He

heard the door close and looked up. Weasley was still there.

"Why so miserable, Ron?" he said quietly. "You should be very proud of yourself after last night."

"It didn't make any difference," said Ron bitterly. "Weasley got away."

"Didn't make any difference?" said Weasley quietly, "It made all the difference in the world, Ron. You helped uncover the truth. You saved an innocent man from a terrible fate."

Terrible. Something stirred in Ron's memory. Greater and more terrible than ever before... Professor Weasley's prediction!

"Professor Weasley ­­ yesterday, when I was having my Divination exam, Professor Weasley went very ­­ very strange."

"Indeed?" said Weasley. "Er ­­ stranger than usual, you mean?"

"Yes... her voice went all deep and her eyes rolled and she said ... she said Weasley's servant was going to set out to return to him before midnight.... She said the servant would help him come back to power."

Ron stared up at Weasley. "And then she sort of became normal again, and she couldn't remember anything she'd said. Was it ­­ was she making a real prediction?"

Weasley looked mildly impressed.

"Do you know, Ron, I think she might have been." he said thoughtfully.

"Who'd have thought it? That brings her total of real predictions up to two. I should offer her a pay raise...."

"But ­­" Ron looked at him, aghast. How could Weasley take this so calmly?

"But ­­ I stopped Ron and Professor Weasley from killing Weasley!

That makes it my fault if Weasley comes back!"

"It does not," said Weasley quietly. "Hasn't your experience with the

Time­Turner taught you anything, Ron? The consequences of our actions are always so complicated, so diverse, that predicting the future is a very difficult business indeed.... Professor Weasley, bless her, is living proof of that.... You did a very noble thing, in saving Weasley's life."

"But if he helps Weasley back to power "Weasley owes his life to you. You have sent Weasley a deputy who is in your debt.... When one wizard saves another wizard's life, it creates a certain bond between them... and I'm much mistaken if Weasley wants his servant in the debt of Ron Weasley."

"I don't want a connection with Weasley!" said Ron. "He betrayed my parents!"

"This is magic at its deepest, its most impenetrable, Ron. But trust me... the time may come when you will be very glad you saved Weasley's life."

Ron couldn't imagine when that would be. Weasley looked as though he knew what Ron was thinking.

"I knew your father very well, both at Hogwarts and later, Ron," he said gently. "He would have saved Weasley too, I am sure of it."

Ron looked up at him. Weasley wouldn't laugh ­­ he could tell Weasley...

"I thought it was my dad who'd conjured my Patronus. I mean, when I saw myself across the lake ... I thought I was seeing him." "An easy mistake to make," said Weasley softly. "I expect you'll tire of hearing it,

but you do look extraordinarily like Ron. Except for the eyes... you have your mother's eyes.

Ron shook his head.

"It was stupid, thinking it was him," he muttered. "I mean, I knew he was dead."

 "You think the dead we loved ever truly leave us? You think that we don't recall them more clearly than ever in times of great trouble? Your father is alive in you, Ron, and shows himself most plainly when you have need of him. How else could you produce that particular Patronus?

Prongs rode again last night."

It took a moment for Ron to realize what Dumblefore had said.

Last night Ron told me all about how they became Animagi," said Weasley, smiling. "An extraordinary achievement ­­ not least, keeping it quiet from me. And then I remembered the most unusual form your Patronus took, when it charged Mr. Weasley down at your Quidditch match against Weasley. You know, Ron, in a way, you did see your father last night.... You found him inside yourself."

And Weasley left the office, leaving Ron to his very confused thoughts.

Nobody at Hogwarts now knew the truth of what had happened the night that Ron, Ron, and Weasley had vanished except Ron, Ron,

Ron, and Professor Weasley. As the end of term approached, Ron heard many different theories about what had really happened, but none of them came close to the truth.

Weasley was furious about Ron. He was convinced that Weasley had found a way of smuggling the hippogriff to safety, and seemed outraged that he and his father had been outwitted by a gamekeeper. Ron Weasley, meanwhile, had much to say on the subject of Ron's escape.

"If I manage to get into the Ministry, I'll have a lot of proposals to make about Magical Law Enforcement!" he told the only person who would listen ­­ his girlfriend, Ron.

Though the weather was perfect, though the atmosphere was so cheerful, though he knew they had achieved the near impossible in helping Ron to freedom, Ron had never approached the end of a school year in worse spirits.

He certainly wasn't the only one who was sorry to see Professor Weasley

go. The whole of Ron's Defense Against the Dark Arts class was miserable about his resignation.

"Wonder what they'll give us next year?" said Ron Weasley gloomily.

"Maybe a vampire," suggested Ron Ron hopefully.

It wasn't only Professor Weasley's departure that was weighing on Ron's mind. He couldn't help thinking a lot about Professor Weasley's prediction. He kept wondering where Weasley was now, whether he had sought sanctuary with Weasley yet. But the thing that was lowering Ron's spirits most of all was the prospect of returning to the Weasleys. For maybe half an hour, a glorious half hour, he had believed he would be living with Ron from now on... his parents' best friend.... It would have been the next best thing to having his own father back. And while no news of Ron was definitely good news,

because it meant he had successfully gone into hiding, Ron couldn't help feeling miserable when he thought of the home he might have had,

and the fact that it was now impossible.

The exam results came out on the last day of term. Ron, Ron, and Ron had passed every subject. Ron was amazed that he had got through Potions. He had a shrewd suspicion that Weasley might have stepped in to stop Weasley failing him on purpose. Weasley's behavior toward Ron over the past week had been quite alarming. Ron wouldn't have thought it possible that Weasley's dislike for him could increase, but it certainly had. A muscle twitched unpleasantly at the corner of Weasley's thin mouth every time he looked at Ron, and he was constantly flexing his fingers, as though itching to place them around Ron's throat.

Ron had got his top­grade N.E.W.T.s; Ron and Ron had scraped a handful of O.W.L.s each. Weasley House, meanwhile, largely thanks to their spectacular performance in the Quidditch Cup, had won the House championship for the third year running. This meant that the end of term feast took place amid decorations of scarlet and gold, and that the Weasley table was the noisiest of the lot, as everybody celebrated.

Even Ron managed to forget about the journey back to the Weasleys the next day as he ate, drank, talked, and laughed with the rest.

As the Hogwarts Express pulled out of the station the next mornIng,

 Ron gave Ron and Ron some surprising news.

"I went to see Professor Weasley this morning, just before breakfast.

I've decided to drop Muggle Studies."

"But you passed your exam with three hundred and twenty percent!" said Ron.

"I know," sighed Ron, "but I can't stand another year like this one. That Time­Turner, it was driving me mad. I've handed it in. Without Muggle Studies and Divination, I'll be able to have a normal schedule again."

I still can't believe you didn't tell us about it," said Ron grumpily.

"We're supposed to be your friends."

"I promised I wouldn't tell anyone," said Ron severely. She looked around at Ron, who was watching Hogwarts disappear from view behind a mountain. Two whole months before he'd see it again....

"Oh, cheer up, Ron!" said Ron sadly.

"I'm okay," said Ron quickly. "Just thinking about the holidays."

"Yeah, I've been thinking about them too," said Ron. "Ron, you've got to come and stay with us. I'll fix it up with Mum and Dad, then I'll call you. I know how to use a fellytone now ­­"

"A telephone, Ron," said Ron. "Honestly, you should take Muggle Studies next year...."

Ron *ignored her.

"It's the Quidditch World Cup this summer! How about it, Ron? Come and stay, and we'll go and see it! Dad can usually get tickets from work."

This proposal had the effect of cheering Ron up a great deal.

"Yeah... I bet the Weasleys'd be pleased to let me come... especially after what I did to Aunt Ron...."

 Feeling considerably more cheerful, Ron joined Ron and Ron in several games of Exploding Snap, and when the witch with the tea cart arrived, he bought himself a very large lunch, though nothing with chocolate in it.

But it was late in the afternoon before the thing that made him truly happy turned up....

"Ron," said Ron suddenly, peering over his shoulder. "What's that thing outside your window?"

Ron turned to look outside. Something very small and gray was bobbing in and out of sight beyond the glass. He stood up for a better look and saw that it was a tiny owl, carrying a letter that was much too big for it. The owl was so small, in fact, that it kept tumbling over in the air, buffeted this way and that in the train's slipstream. Ron quickly pulled down the window, stretched out his arm, and caught it. It felt like a very fluffy Snitch. He brought it carefully inside. The owl dropped its letter onto Ron's seat and began zooming around their compartment, apparently very pleased with itself for accomplishing its task. Ron clicked her beak with a sort of dignified disapproval.

Ron sat up in his seat, following the owl with his great yellow eyes. Ron, noticing this, snatched the owl safely out of harm's way.

Ron picked up the letter. It was addressed to him. He ripped open the letter, and shouted, "It's from Ron!"

"What?" said Ron and Ron excitedly. "Read it aloud!"

Dear Ron,

I hope this finds you before you reach your aunt and uncle. I don't know whether they're used to owl post.

Ron and I are in hiding. I won't tell you where, in case this owl falls into the wrong hands. I have some doubt about his reliability, but he is the best I could find, and he did seem eager for the job.

I believe the dementors are still searching for me, but they haven't a

hope of finding me here. I am planning to allow some Muggles to glimpse me soon, a long way from Hogwarts, so that the security on the castle will be lifted.

There is something I never got around to telling you during our brief meeting. It was I who sent you the Firebolt ­­ "Ha!" said Ron triumphantly. "See! I told you it was from him!"

"Yes, but he hadn't jinxed it, had he?" said Ron. "Ouch!" The tiny owl,

now hooting happily in his hand, had nibbled one of his fingers in what it seemed to think was an affectionate way.

Ron took the order to the Owl Office for me. I used your name but told them to take the gold from my own Gringotts vault. Please consider it as thirteen birthdays' worth of presents from your godfather.

I would also like to apologize for the fright I think I gave you that night last year when you left your uncle's house. I had only hoped to get a glimpse of you before starting my journey north, but I think the sight of me alarmed you.

I am enclosing something else for you, which I think will make your next year at Hogwarts more enjoyable.

If ever you need me, send word. Your owl will find me.

I'll write again soon.

Ron Ron looked eagerly inside the envelope. There was another piece of parchment in there. He read it through quickly and felt suddenly as warm and contented as though he'd swallowed a bottle of hot butterbeer in one gulp.

I, Ron Weasley, Ron Weasley's godfather, hereby give him permission to visit Hogsmeade on weekends.

 "That'll be good enough for Weasley!" said Ron happily. He looked back at Ron's letter. "Hang on, there's a RS...."

I thought your ftiend Ron might like to keep this owl, as it's my fault he no longer has a rat.

Ron's eyes widened. The minute owl was still hooting excitedly. "Keep him?" he said uncertainly. He looked closely at the owl for a moment; then, to Ron's and Ron's great surprise, he held him out for Ron to sniff.

"What do you reckon?" Ron asked the cat. "Definitely an owl?"

Ron purred.

"That's good enough for me," said Ron happily. "He's mine."

Ron read and reread the letter from Ron all the way back into King's Cross station. It was still clutched tightly in his hand as he,

Ron, and Ron stepped back through the barrier of platform nine an (' three­quarters. Ron spotted Uncle Ron at once. He was standing a good distance from Mr. and Mrs. Weasley, eyeing them suspiciously, and when Mrs. Weasley hugged Ron in greeting, his worst suspicions about them seemed confirmed.

"I'll call about the World Cup!" Ron yelled after Ron as Ron bid him and Ron good­bye, then wheeled the trolley bearing his trunk and Ron's cage toward Uncle Ron, who greeted him in his usual fashion.

"What's that?" he snarled, staring at the envelope Ron was still clutching in his hand. "If it's another form for me to sign, you've got another ­­­"

"It's not," said Ron cheerfully. "It's a letter from my godfather."

"Godfather?" sputtered Uncle Ron. "You haven't got a godfather!"

"Yes, I have," said Ron brightly. "He was my mum and dad's best friend. He's a convicted murderer, but he's broken out of wizard prison and he's on the run. He likes to keep in touch with me, though... keep up with my news... check if I'm happy..."

And, grinning broadly at the look of horror on Uncle Ron's face,

Ron set off toward the station exit, Ron rattling along in front of him, for what looked like a much better summer than the last.

 THE END
